Distinguishing المطلقة العامة and المشروطة العامة
Commentator distinguishes two conditional types by description's role.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the absolute general (المطلقة العامة) and the conditional general (المشروطة العامة) by identifying the role of the description in the duration of the predicate.

Core Idea
The difference lies in whether the description actively conditions the predicate's duration.

This passage from the commentary on Yazdi's Hashiya clarifies a subtle but crucial distinction between two types of conditional propositions. While both involve a description like 'as long as he is a writer,' the conditional general (المشروطة العامة) implies that the description has a role in the predication, whereas the absolute general (المطلقة العامة) does not. Mastering this distinction is key to correctly interpreting modal propositions in Islamic logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two proposition types
Focus on the terms المطلقة العامة and المشروطة العامة. The passage states that they are not equivalent, as their negations differ in scope.
2
Compare their negations
The author shows that if they were equal, their negations would also be equal. But since one negation is more general than the other, the original types must differ.
This is an immediate inference about equality and negation.
3
Examine the role of description in duration
In المشروطة العامة, the description (e.g., 'writer') is considered to have an influence on the duration of the predicate (e.g., 'moving fingers'). In المطلقة العامة, no such influence is assumed.
The passage says: 'they consider duration with the condition of the description and as long as the description' for المشروطة.
4
Apply to an Islamic example
Consider 'Every praying person is in a state of purification as long as he is praying.' In المشروطة العامة, the prayer actively conditions the purification; in المطلقة العامة, it simply holds during the prayer without dependence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الدائمة و هو حواشي الحاشية المطلقة العامة كما صرح به غير واحد ولو كانتا متساويتين تلزم ان يكون نقيضا الاعم والاخص مطلقا متساويين وقد سبق ان بين نقيضيها ايضاً عموماً مطلقا لكن بعكس العينين. وبعبارة اخرى أوضح من ذلك لو كانتا متساويتين للزم ان يكون نقيضا هما ايضاً متساويين على ما سبق تحقيقه والحال أن بينهما عموماً مطلقا كما ذكر. نعم قد يطلق الضرورة على استحالة انفكاك شيء عن شيء مطلقا فتسمى الضرورة بالمعنى الاعم كالاول بالمعنى الاخص لكن ليس ذلك بمرادهم فى مبحث القضاياء بدليل ذكر هم الدوام في مقابله و الى ما ذكرنا اشار المحشى حيث قال: «و ان لم يكن مستحيلاً». (میرزا محمد علی) (۸۱) قوله : مادام الوصف العنواني ثابتاً لتلك الذات»: لا يذهب عليك انهم لم يعتبروا هنا معنيين كما اعتبروا في المشروطة العامة بان يعتبروا الدوام بشرط الوصف و مادام الوصف و ذلك لان الدوام كما ذكر عدم انفكاك الشيء عن الشيء فحينئذ لا يتفاوت الحال بين ان يكون للوصف مدخل في دوام المحمول للموضوع كما في قولنا: (بالدوام كل كاتب متحرك الاصابع مادام كاتباً أو لم يكن كما في قولنا : «بالدوام كل كاتب حيوان مادام كاتباً فان المحمول اذا كان دائماً لمجموع الذات والوصف كان دائما للذات في جميع اوقات الوصف فتأمل. (میراز محمد علی) (۸۲) اذا اطلقت نحو: «لاشيء من الكاتب بساكن الاصابع مادام كاتباً فهم اهل العرف ان نسبة ساكن الاصابع مسلوب عن الكاتب مادام كاتيا . الامراء (۸۳) قوله: «بل من الموجبة ايضاً »: اشارة الى ان ما يستفاد من بعض المحققين في شرح الرسالة وغيره من تخصيص فهم العرف هذا المعنى بالسالبة، ليس بجيد فان العرف كما يفهم هذا المعنى من السالبة فكذا يفهم من الموجبة أيضاً فلا حاجة لتخصيصه بالسالبة. و في اطلاق الموجبة و عدم تقييدها بمعدولة المحمول و كذا فى اطلاق السائبة و عدم تقييدها بكونها غير معدولة المحمول اشارة الى ان ماربما يتوهم هنا كما اتفق لبعض المحققين من المحشين في شرح الكلام من ان فهم العرف هذا المعنى و ان كان غير مختص بالسالبة بل كما يفهم منها، يفهم من الموجبة أيضاً لكن لا مطلقا بل اذا كانت فى معنى السالبة كما اذا كانت معدولة المحمول كقولنا : «كل نائم غير مستيقظ» و كذا ليس في مطلق السالبة، بل اذا لم تكن في معنى الموجبة والا كما اذا كانت معدولة المحمول مثل قولنا : «لاشيء من الكاتب بلا حيوان فلا يفهم هذا المعنى ، ليس كما ينبغى بل العرف لا يفرق بين الموجبة و السالبة المعدولة المحمول و بين غير هما فى فهم هذا المعنى ويفهمه في الموجبة و ان لم تكن معدولة المحمول وفى السالبة و ان كانت معدولة كما هو ظاهر، هذا. واظن ان الذي أوقعهم في ذلك ظهور فهم هذا المعنى في السائبة بناء على القاعدة المقررة عند ارباب المعانى المذكورة آنفاً فاته اذا قلنا: لاشيء من النائم بمستيقظ فالنفى يفيد سلب المستيقظ من النائم وثبوته للشخص وذلك معنى الدوام الوصفى وخفائه فى الموجبة بناء على توهم عدم ثبوت تلك القاعدة فيها وانت خبير بان هذه القاعدة و ان كانت مشهورة فى النقي الا ان الاثبات ايضاً كذلك. قال الشيخ عبد القاهر البيانى فى دلائل الاعجاز ان النفى اذادخل على كلام فيه تقييد بوجه ما يتوجه الى ذلك القيد وكذلك الاثبات وجملة الامر انه ما من كلام فيه امر زايد على مجرد اثبات الشيء للشيء أو نفيه عنه الا و هو الغرض الخاص والمقصود من الكلام وهذا مما لا سبيل الى الشك فيه انتهى . فاذا قلنا : كل كاتب متحرك الاصابع مثلاً وهو فى معنى كل شخص كاتب متحرك الاصابع كان المعنى اثبات تحرك الاصابع للكاتب لا الشخص، نعم فرق بين الايجاب والنفي من حيث ان النفي يفيد ثبوت اصل الحكم والاثبات لا يفيد نفى اصل الحكم وهذا القدر لا يوجب اختصاص فهم العرف هذا المعنى بالسالبة دون الموجبة فتقطن. ثم يظهر من بعض المحققين ان فهم هذا المعنى انما هو فيا اذا كان للوصف مدخل في الدوام كقولنا : كل كاتب متحرك الاصابع ولاشيء من الكاتب بساكن الاصابع واما اذا لم يكن له مدخل فيه فلا ، كقولنا كل كاتب حيوان ولاشيء من وقد ظهر لك مما تلوناه ان كون الوصف دخيلاً في الدوام ليس له مدخل في فهم العرف هذا المعنى، بل كما يفهم هذا المعنى من نحو كل كاتب متحرك الاصابع فكذا يفهم من نحو: «كل كاتب الكاتب بحجر. ثابتة له مطلقا فهو شي حيوان ان الحيوانية ثابتة للموضوع مادام كاتباً وما يترأى في الخارج من انها ثابر آخر وكلامنا في دلالة اللفظ من حيث هو هو من غير نظر إلى النسبة الخارجية فتأمل. (ميرزا محمد علی) (۸۴) اى عند عدم ذكر الجهة فى القضية الموجبة والسالبة، لا في الموجبة فقط كما هو المتبادر من كلامه : لوم اسلامی ثم اعلم انهم لم يعتبروا للعرفية معنيين على قياس معنى المشروطة اذ الحال بالنسبة الى الضرورة يتفاوت بين الحكم بثبوت المحمول المجموع الذات والوصف العنواني و بين الحكم بثبوته للذات في زمان ذلك الوصف على مالوحنا اليه بخلاف الحال بالنسبة الى الدوام فانه لا تفاوت بين الحكمين فيه اذ كل مادة صدق فيها الحكم بدوام ثبوت المحمول لمجموع الذات والوصف يصدق فيها الحكم بدوامه في زمان ذلك الوصف فلم يحصل للعرفية معنيان بل لها معنى واحد اعنى الحكم بدوام ثبوت المحمول لمجموع الذات و الوصف ففى العرفية لا يتيسر ان يكون للوصف مدخل فى دوام ثبوت المحمول بالمعنى المذكور في المشروطة لان الدوام كما يتحقق بالنسبة الى مجموع الذات والوصف يتحقق بالنسبة الى الذات وحده في زمان ذلك الوصف فلا يصح ان يقال: لولم يعتبر الوصف مع الذات مركباً لم يتحقق الدوام. (عبد الرحيم )
The perpetual and it is the commentary on the commentary: the absolute general (المطلقة العامة) as stated by more than one. And if they were equal, it would necessitate that the negations of the more general and the more specific absolutely are equal, and it has preceded that between their two negations there is also absolute generality, but with the reverse of the two. In other words, clearer than that: if they were equal, it would necessitate that their two negations are also equal, according to the verification that preceded, while the state is that between them there is absolute generality as mentioned. Yes, necessity (الضرورة) may be applied to the impossibility of something separating from something absolutely, so it is called necessity in the more general sense like the first in the more specific sense, but that is not what they intend in the discussion of propositions, because they mention duration in contrast to it. And to what we mentioned, the commentator pointed when he said: 'even if it is not impossible'. (Mirza Muhammad 'Ali) (81) His statement: 'as long as the attributive description is established for that essence': It should not escape you that they did not consider two meanings here as they considered in the conditional general (المشروطة العامة) where they consider duration with the condition of the description and as long as the description, because duration, as mentioned, is the non-separation of a thing from a thing. Therefore, the situation does not differ between the description having an influence on the duration of the predicate for the subject, as in our statement: (with duration) 'Every writer is moving his fingers as long as he is a writer', or not having, as in our statement: 'with duration every writer is an animal as long as he is a writer'. For if the predicate is perpetual for the combination of essence and description, it is perpetual for the essence in all times of the description. So reflect. (Mirza Muhammad 'Ali) (82) When we utter something like: 'Nothing of the writer is still in fingers as long as he is a writer', the people of common understanding (العرف) understand that the relation of still in fingers is negated of the writer as long as he is a writer. (83) His statement: 'rather from the affirmative also': an indication that what is understood from some investigators in the commentary on the treatise and others, that the common understanding of this meaning is specific to the negative, is not good. For common understanding, as it understands this meaning from the negative, so too it understands from the affirmative also, so there is no need to specify it to the negative. And in the unrestricted use of the affirmative and its lack of restriction to a modified predicate, and likewise in the unrestricted use of the negative and its lack of restriction to its being non-modified predicate, there is an indication that what might be imagined here, as happened to some investigators among the commenters in the explanation of the speech—that the common understanding of this meaning, even if not specific to the negative, rather as understood from it, is understood from the affirmative also, but not absolutely, rather when it is in the meaning of the negative, as when it has a modified predicate like our statement: 'Every sleeper is not awake', and likewise it is not in the absolute negative, rather if it is not in the meaning of the affirmative, otherwise as when it has a modified predicate such as our statement: 'Nothing of the writer is without animal', then it does not understand this meaning—is not as it should be. Rather, common understanding does not differentiate between the affirmative and negative with modified predicate and between other than them in understanding this meaning, and understands it in the affirmative even if it does not have a modified predicate, and in the negative even if it has a modified predicate, as is apparent. This. And I think that what caused them to fall into that is the apparent understanding of this meaning in the negative based on the rule established among the masters of meanings mentioned earlier. For if we say: 'Nothing of the sleeper is awake', then the negation conveys the negation of 'awake' from the sleeper and its affirmation for the person, and that is the meaning of temporal duration (الدوام الوصفي), and its being hidden in the affirmative is based on the illusion that this rule is not established in it. And you are well aware that this rule, even if it is famous in negation, yet affirmation is also like that. Sheikh 'Abd al-Qahir al-Bayani said in The Proofs of Inimitability: 'Negation, when it enters into speech containing a restriction in any way, is directed to that restriction, and likewise affirmation. And the sum of the matter is that any speech containing something additional to mere affirmation of something for something or negation of it from it, that is the specific purpose and intention of the speech, and this is something not subject to doubt.' End of quote. So if we say: 'Every writer is moving his fingers', for example, and it is in the meaning of 'every person who is a writer is moving his fingers', the meaning is the affirmation of movement of fingers for the writer, not the person. Yes, there is a difference between affirmation and negation in that negation conveys the establishment of the original judgment, while affirmation does not convey the negation of the original judgment. And this much does not necessitate the specification of the common understanding of this meaning to the negative without the affirmative. So be attentive. Then some investigators showed that this meaning is only understood when the description has influence on the duration, like our statement: 'Every writer is moving his fingers' and 'Nothing of the writer is still in fingers'. But when it has no influence, then not, like our statement: 'Every writer is an animal' and 'Nothing of the writer is a stone.' And it has become apparent to you from what we recited that the description being influential in duration has no influence on the common understanding of this meaning. Rather, as this meaning is understood from 'every writer is moving his fingers', so too is it understood from 'every writer is an animal'—that animality is established for the subject as long as he is a writer. And what appears externally—that it is established for him absolutely—is another matter, and our speech is about the indication of the word as such, without regard to external relation. So reflect. (Mirza Muhammad 'Ali) (84) That is, when the modality is not mentioned in the affirmative and negative proposition, not in the affirmative only as might be understood from his statement: 'Islam...' Then know that they did not consider for the conditional common (العرفية) two meanings on the pattern of the meaning of the conditional general (المشروطة), because the situation with respect to necessity differs between the judgment of establishing the predicate for the combination of essence and the attributive description and the judgment of establishing it for the essence in the time of that description, as we hinted at. Contrary to the situation with respect to duration, for there is no difference between the two judgments in it, because every material in which the judgment of the duration of the predicate's establishment for the combination of essence and description is true, the judgment of its duration in the time of that description is also true. Thus the conditional common (العرفية) does not acquire two meanings; rather it has one meaning, i.e., the judgment of the duration of the predicate's establishment for the combination of essence and description. So in the conditional common (العرفية), it is not possible for the description to have influence on the duration of the predicate's establishment in the sense mentioned in the conditional general (المشروطة), because duration, as it is realized in relation to the combination of essence and description, is realized in relation to the essence alone in the time of that description. So it is not correct to say: If the description were not considered together with the essence as a composite, the duration would not be realized. (Abd al-Rahim)
Source pages p. 283

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the distinction between two types of conditional propositions in Islamic logic: the absolute general (المطلقة العامة) and the conditional general (المشروطة العامة). The author begins by noting that if these two were equivalent, their negations would also be equivalent, but this is not the case. He then clarifies that the term 'necessity' (الضرورة) is sometimes used broadly to mean absolute inseparability, but in the context of propositions, it is contrasted with 'duration' (الدوام) which refers to the non-separation of a thing from another as long as a certain condition holds. The core of the discussion concerns the concept of 'temporal duration' (الدوام الوصفي) in propositions that involve a description (الوصف العنواني) like 'as long as he is a writer' (مادام كاتباً). The commentator emphasizes that common sense (العرف) understands both positive and negative propositions with such a description in the same way: the predicate is affirmed or denied of the subject only during the time the description applies. For example, 'Every writer is moving his fingers as long as he is a writer' is understood as the movement occurring only during the writing state, and similarly 'Nothing of the writer is still in fingers as long as he is a writer' is understood as the stillness being negated only during that state. The commentator argues against a view held by some investigators that this understanding is exclusive to negative propositions or to cases where the predicate depends on the description. He supports his argument with a quote from Sheikh Abd al-Qahir al-Bayani, who affirms that both negation and affirmation, when they enter a statement with a restriction, are directed to that restriction. He concludes that the conditional common (العرفية) has only one meaning: the judgment of the duration of the predicate's establishment for the combination of essence and description, unlike the conditional general (المشروطة) where two meanings are possible. The key takeaway is that in the العرفية, the description cannot have a special influence on the duration because duration is realized equally for the combination and for the essence alone during the time of the description.

Key Terms

المشروطة العامة
الدوام الوصفي

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if المطلقة العامة and المشروطة العامة were equivalent, what would follow?
A) Their negations would be equivalent.
B) Their negations would be different.
C) They would have identical definitions.
D) The description would have no role.

Key Takeaway
المطلقة العامة and المشروطة العامة are distinct because the latter involves the description actively conditioning the predicate's duration, while the former does not.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify which of the following is an example of المطلقة العامة and which is المشروطة العامة: (a) 'Every student is attentive as long as the teacher is present.' (b) 'Every student is human as long as the student is a student.' Explain your reasoning based on the role of the description in duration.

Immediate Inference
intermediate

Common Understanding of Temporal Duration in Conditionals
Commentator argues for equal temporal interpretation in affirmatives and negatives.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why common sense (العرف) understands both affirmative and negative conditional propositions as implying temporal duration, and refute the view that this is limited to negatives.

Core Idea
Common sense treats both affirmation and negation equally when a temporal description is present.

In this part of the commentary, the author addresses a widespread misconception: that only negative propositions with a description are understood temporally. By drawing on the principles of Arabic rhetoric and citing al-Bayani, he shows that affirmation also carries the same implication. This lesson will equip you to recognize this principle in various examples and apply it to Islamic texts.

Guided Path
1
Read the example propositions
The author gives 'Every writer is moving his fingers as long as he is a writer' (affirmative) and 'Nothing of the writer is still in fingers as long as he is a writer' (negative). Note the temporal phrase 'as long as he is a writer'.
2
Identify the understanding of common people
Common sense understands that in both cases, the predicate holds only during the time the description applies. For the affirmative, movement occurs only while writing; for the negative, stillness is negated only during writing.
3
Analyze the objection by some investigators
Some claimed that this understanding is only for negatives, or only for affirmatives when the predicate is modified. The author refutes this using al-Bayani's rule that restriction in speech applies to both affirmation and negation equally.
Al-Bayani's quote: negation and affirmation when entering a restricted statement both target the same restriction.
4
Apply to an Islamic example
Consider 'Every fasting person is abstaining from food as long as he is fasting.' Apply the principle: does common sense understand this as temporary? What about the negative 'No fasting person is eating as long as he is fasting'? Both are understood temporally.

الدائمة و هو حواشي الحاشية المطلقة العامة كما صرح به غير واحد ولو كانتا متساويتين تلزم ان يكون نقيضا الاعم والاخص مطلقا متساويين وقد سبق ان بين نقيضيها ايضاً عموماً مطلقا لكن بعكس العينين. وبعبارة اخرى أوضح من ذلك لو كانتا متساويتين للزم ان يكون نقيضا هما ايضاً متساويين على ما سبق تحقيقه والحال أن بينهما عموماً مطلقا كما ذكر. نعم قد يطلق الضرورة على استحالة انفكاك شيء عن شيء مطلقا فتسمى الضرورة بالمعنى الاعم كالاول بالمعنى الاخص لكن ليس ذلك بمرادهم فى مبحث القضاياء بدليل ذكر هم الدوام في مقابله و الى ما ذكرنا اشار المحشى حيث قال: «و ان لم يكن مستحيلاً». (میراز محمد علی) (۸۲) اذا اطلقت نحو: «لاشيء من الكاتب بساكن الاصابع مادام كاتباً فهم اهل العرف ان نسبة ساكن الاصابع مسلوب عن الكاتب مادام كاتيا . الامراء (۸۳) قوله: «بل من الموجبة ايضاً »: اشارة الى ان ما يستفاد من بعض المحققين في شرح الرسالة وغيره من تخصيص فهم العرف هذا المعنى بالسالبة، ليس بجيد فان العرف كما يفهم هذا المعنى من السالبة فكذا يفهم من الموجبة أيضاً فلا حاجة لتخصيصه بالسالبة. و في اطلاق الموجبة و عدم تقييدها بمعدولة المحمول و كذا فى اطلاق السائبة و عدم تقييدها بكونها غير معدولة المحمول اشارة الى ان ماربما يتوهم هنا كما اتفق لبعض المحققين من المحشين في شرح الكلام من ان فهم العرف هذا المعنى و ان كان غير مختص بالسالبة بل كما يفهم منها، يفهم من الموجبة أيضاً لكن لا مطلقا بل اذا كانت فى معنى السالبة كما اذا كانت معدولة المحمول كقولنا : «كل نائم غير مستيقظ» و كذا ليس في مطلق السالبة، بل اذا لم تكن في معنى الموجبة والا كما اذا كانت معدولة المحمول مثل قولنا : «لاشيء من الكاتب بلا حيوان فلا يفهم هذا المعنى ، ليس كما ينبغى بل العرف لا يفرق بين الموجبة و السالبة المعدولة المحمول و بين غير هما فى فهم هذا المعنى ويفهمه في الموجبة و ان لم تكن معدولة المحمول وفى السالبة و ان كانت معدولة كما هو ظاهر، هذا. واظن ان الذي أوقعهم في ذلك ظهور فهم هذا المعنى في السائبة بناء على القاعدة المقررة عند ارباب المعانى المذكورة آنفاً فاته اذا قلنا: لاشيء من النائم بمستيقظ فالنفى يفيد سلب المستيقظ من النائم وثبوته للشخص وذلك معنى الدوام الوصفى وخفائه فى الموجبة بناء على توهم عدم ثبوت تلك القاعدة فيها وانت خبير بان هذه القاعدة و ان كانت مشهورة فى النقي الا ان الاثبات ايضاً كذلك. قال الشيخ عبد القاهر البيانى فى دلائل الاعجاز ان النفى اذادخل على كلام فيه تقييد بوجه ما يتوجه الى ذلك القيد وكذلك الاثبات وجملة الامر انه ما من كلام فيه امر زايد على مجرد اثبات الشيء للشيء أو نفيه عنه الا و هو الغرض الخاص والمقصود من الكلام وهذا مما لا سبيل الى الشك فيه انتهى . فاذا قلنا : كل كاتب متحرك الاصابع مثلاً وهو فى معنى كل شخص كاتب متحرك الاصابع كان المعنى اثبات تحرك الاصابع للكاتب لا الشخص، نعم فرق بين الايجاب والنفي من حيث ان النفي يفيد ثبوت اصل الحكم والاثبات لا يفيد نفى اصل الحكم وهذا القدر لا يوجب اختصاص فهم العرف هذا المعنى بالسالبة دون الموجبة فتقطن. ثم يظهر من بعض المحققين ان فهم هذا المعنى انما هو فيا اذا كان للوصف مدخل في الدوام كقولنا : كل كاتب متحرك الاصابع ولاشيء من الكاتب بساكن الاصابع واما اذا لم يكن له مدخل فيه فلا ، كقولنا كل كاتب حيوان ولاشيء من وقد ظهر لك مما تلوناه ان كون الوصف دخيلاً في الدوام ليس له مدخل في فهم العرف هذا المعنى، بل كما يفهم هذا المعنى من نحو كل كاتب متحرك الاصابع فكذا يفهم من نحو: «كل كاتب الكاتب بحجر. ثابتة له مطلقا فهو شي حيوان ان الحيوانية ثابتة للموضوع مادام كاتباً وما يترأى في الخارج من انها ثابر آخر وكلامنا في دلالة اللفظ من حيث هو هو من غير نظر إلى النسبة الخارجية فتأمل. (ميرزا محمد علی) (۸۴) اى عند عدم ذكر الجهة فى القضية الموجبة والسالبة، لا في الموجبة فقط كما هو المتبادر من كلامه : لوم اسلامی ثم اعلم انهم لم يعتبروا للعرفية معنيين على قياس معنى المشروطة اذ الحال بالنسبة الى الضرورة يتفاوت بين الحكم بثبوت المحمول المجموع الذات والوصف العنواني و بين الحكم بثبوته للذات في زمان ذلك الوصف على مالوحنا اليه بخلاف الحال بالنسبة الى الدوام فانه لا تفاوت بين الحكمين فيه اذ كل مادة صدق فيها الحكم بدوام ثبوت المحمول لمجموع الذات والوصف يصدق فيها الحكم بدوامه في زمان ذلك الوصف فلم يحصل للعرفية معنيان بل لها معنى واحد اعنى الحكم بدوام ثبوت المحمول لمجموع الذات و الوصف ففى العرفية لا يتيسر ان يكون للوصف مدخل فى دوام ثبوت المحمول بالمعنى المذكور في المشروطة لان الدوام كما يتحقق بالنسبة الى مجموع الذات والوصف يتحقق بالنسبة الى الذات وحده في زمان ذلك الوصف فلا يصح ان يقال: لولم يعتبر الوصف مع الذات مركباً لم يتحقق الدوام. (عبد الرحيم )
The perpetual and it is the commentary on the commentary: the absolute general (المطلقة العامة) as stated by more than one. And if they were equal, it would necessitate that the negations of the more general and the more specific absolutely are equal, and it has preceded that between their two negations there is also absolute generality, but with the reverse of the two. In other words, clearer than that: if they were equal, it would necessitate that their two negations are also equal, according to the verification that preceded, while the state is that between them there is absolute generality as mentioned. Yes, necessity (الضرورة) may be applied to the impossibility of something separating from something absolutely, so it is called necessity in the more general sense like the first in the more specific sense, but that is not what they intend in the discussion of propositions, because they mention duration in contrast to it. And to what we mentioned, the commentator pointed when he said: 'even if it is not impossible'. (Mirza Muhammad 'Ali) (81) His statement: 'as long as the attributive description is established for that essence': It should not escape you that they did not consider two meanings here as they considered in the conditional general (المشروطة العامة) where they consider duration with the condition of the description and as long as the description, because duration, as mentioned, is the non-separation of a thing from a thing. Therefore, the situation does not differ between the description having an influence on the duration of the predicate for the subject, as in our statement: (with duration) 'Every writer is moving his fingers as long as he is a writer', or not having, as in our statement: 'with duration every writer is an animal as long as he is a writer'. For if the predicate is perpetual for the combination of essence and description, it is perpetual for the essence in all times of the description. So reflect. (Mirza Muhammad 'Ali) (82) When we utter something like: 'Nothing of the writer is still in fingers as long as he is a writer', the people of common understanding (العرف) understand that the relation of still in fingers is negated of the writer as long as he is a writer. (83) His statement: 'rather from the affirmative also': an indication that what is understood from some investigators in the commentary on the treatise and others, that the common understanding of this meaning is specific to the negative, is not good. For common understanding, as it understands this meaning from the negative, so too it understands from the affirmative also, so there is no need to specify it to the negative. And in the unrestricted use of the affirmative and its lack of restriction to a modified predicate, and likewise in the unrestricted use of the negative and its lack of restriction to its being non-modified predicate, there is an indication that what might be imagined here, as happened to some investigators among the commenters in the explanation of the speech—that the common understanding of this meaning, even if not specific to the negative, rather as understood from it, is understood from the affirmative also, but not absolutely, rather when it is in the meaning of the negative, as when it has a modified predicate like our statement: 'Every sleeper is not awake', and likewise it is not in the absolute negative, rather if it is not in the meaning of the affirmative, otherwise as when it has a modified predicate such as our statement: 'Nothing of the writer is without animal', then it does not understand this meaning—is not as it should be. Rather, common understanding does not differentiate between the affirmative and negative with modified predicate and between other than them in understanding this meaning, and understands it in the affirmative even if it does not have a modified predicate, and in the negative even if it has a modified predicate, as is apparent. This. And I think that what caused them to fall into that is the apparent understanding of this meaning in the negative based on the rule established among the masters of meanings mentioned earlier. For if we say: 'Nothing of the sleeper is awake', then the negation conveys the negation of 'awake' from the sleeper and its affirmation for the person, and that is the meaning of temporal duration (الدوام الوصفي), and its being hidden in the affirmative is based on the illusion that this rule is not established in it. And you are well aware that this rule, even if it is famous in negation, yet affirmation is also like that. Sheikh 'Abd al-Qahir al-Bayani said in The Proofs of Inimitability: 'Negation, when it enters into speech containing a restriction in any way, is directed to that restriction, and likewise affirmation. And the sum of the matter is that any speech containing something additional to mere affirmation of something for something or negation of it from it, that is the specific purpose and intention of the speech, and this is something not subject to doubt.' End of quote. So if we say: 'Every writer is moving his fingers', for example, and it is in the meaning of 'every person who is a writer is moving his fingers', the meaning is the affirmation of movement of fingers for the writer, not the person. Yes, there is a difference between affirmation and negation in that negation conveys the establishment of the original judgment, while affirmation does not convey the negation of the original judgment. And this much does not necessitate the specification of the common understanding of this meaning to the negative without the affirmative. So be attentive. Then some investigators showed that this meaning is only understood when the description has influence on the duration, like our statement: 'Every writer is moving his fingers' and 'Nothing of the writer is still in fingers'. But when it has no influence, then not, like our statement: 'Every writer is an animal' and 'Nothing of the writer is a stone.' And it has become apparent to you from what we recited that the description being influential in duration has no influence on the common understanding of this meaning. Rather, as this meaning is understood from 'every writer is moving his fingers', so too is it understood from 'every writer is an animal'—that animality is established for the subject as long as he is a writer. And what appears externally—that it is established for him absolutely—is another matter, and our speech is about the indication of the word as such, without regard to external relation. So reflect. (Mirza Muhammad 'Ali) (84) That is, when the modality is not mentioned in the affirmative and negative proposition, not in the affirmative only as might be understood from his statement: 'Islam...' Then know that they did not consider for the conditional common (العرفية) two meanings on the pattern of the meaning of the conditional general (المشروطة), because the situation with respect to necessity differs between the judgment of establishing the predicate for the combination of essence and the attributive description and the judgment of establishing it for the essence in the time of that description, as we hinted at. Contrary to the situation with respect to duration, for there is no difference between the two judgments in it, because every material in which the judgment of the duration of the predicate's establishment for the combination of essence and description is true, the judgment of its duration in the time of that description is also true. Thus the conditional common (العرفية) does not acquire two meanings; rather it has one meaning, i.e., the judgment of the duration of the predicate's establishment for the combination of essence and description. So in the conditional common (العرفية), it is not possible for the description to have influence on the duration of the predicate's establishment in the sense mentioned in the conditional general (المشروطة), because duration, as it is realized in relation to the combination of essence and description, is realized in relation to the essence alone in the time of that description. So it is not correct to say: If the description were not considered together with the essence as a composite, the duration would not be realized. (Abd al-Rahim)
Source pages p. 283

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the distinction between two types of conditional propositions in Islamic logic: the absolute general (المطلقة العامة) and the conditional general (المشروطة العامة). The author begins by noting that if these two were equivalent, their negations would also be equivalent, but this is not the case. He then clarifies that the term 'necessity' (الضرورة) is sometimes used broadly to mean absolute inseparability, but in the context of propositions, it is contrasted with 'duration' (الدوام) which refers to the non-separation of a thing from another as long as a certain condition holds. The core of the discussion concerns the concept of 'temporal duration' (الدوام الوصفي) in propositions that involve a description (الوصف العنواني) like 'as long as he is a writer' (مادام كاتباً). The commentator emphasizes that common sense (العرف) understands both positive and negative propositions with such a description in the same way: the predicate is affirmed or denied of the subject only during the time the description applies. For example, 'Every writer is moving his fingers as long as he is a writer' is understood as the movement occurring only during the writing state, and similarly 'Nothing of the writer is still in fingers as long as he is a writer' is understood as the stillness being negated only during that state. The commentator argues against a view held by some investigators that this understanding is exclusive to negative propositions or to cases where the predicate depends on the description. He supports his argument with a quote from Sheikh Abd al-Qahir al-Bayani, who affirms that both negation and affirmation, when they enter a statement with a restriction, are directed to that restriction. He concludes that the conditional common (العرفية) has only one meaning: the judgment of the duration of the predicate's establishment for the combination of essence and description, unlike the conditional general (المشروطة) where two meanings are possible. The key takeaway is that in the العرفية, the description cannot have a special influence on the duration because duration is realized equally for the combination and for the essence alone during the time of the description.

Key Terms
الدوام الوصفي
العرفية
العرف
الموجبة
السالبة

Checkpoint

A) It is specific to negative propositions.
B) It is specific to affirmative propositions.
C) It applies only when the predicate depends on the description.
D) It applies only to propositions with a modified predicate.

Key Takeaway
Common sense understands that a temporal description restricts the predicate's duration in both affirmative and negative propositions, as established by the principles of Arabic rhetoric.

Difference in Quantity is Conditional for Contradiction
Commentator explains that the condition of differing in quantity applies only to quantified propositions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when the condition of difference in quantity applies for contradiction between propositions, distinguishing between quantified and unquantified cases.

Core Idea
Difference in quantity is only necessary for contradiction between quantified propositions.

In logical contradiction, two propositions must differ in quality or quantity. But does difference in quantity always matter? This passage from the commentary clarifies a key nuance: the requirement of differing in quantity is not absolute; it applies only when both propositions are quantified. This prevents a common misunderstanding and sharpens your ability to analyze contradictory pairs in Islamic logical arguments.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
The commentator addresses an implicit objection: why don't two particular propositions (e.g., 'Some A is B' and 'Some A is not B') contradict? Because their concepts involve only some individuals, not all.
The concept of a particular proposition does not cover all individuals of the subject.
2
Grasp the answer about subject essence
The answer is that in universal and particular propositions, the essence of the subject differs (all vs. some), so contradiction exists between them. Specifying the subject is external to the concept.
The universal and particular propositions differ in quantity and can be contradictory.
3
See the expansion to other proposition types
The commentator notes that the author's phrase 'if they were quantified' indicates that contradiction is not restricted to quantified propositions; it also occurs in indefinite and personal propositions.
Indefinite (muhmalāt) and personal (shakhṣiyāt) propositions have contradictions without quantity difference.
4
Apply the conditional constraint
Thus, the condition of difference in quantity applies only when both propositions are quantified. In other cases, contradiction can happen without quantity difference.
This prevents the mistake of requiring quantity difference for all contradictions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اجيب بان النظر في جميع الاحكام انما هو الى مفهوم القضية و لما لوحظ مفهوم الجزئيتين وهو الايجاب لبعض الافراد والسلب عن البعض لم يتناقضا واما تعيين الموضوع فامر خارج عن المفهوم و كيف وذات الموضوع فى الكلية جميع الافراد و في الجزئية بعضها مع وجود التناقض بينها، هذا. ثم انما قال: «لو كانتا محصورتين» اشارة الى ان التناقض ليس بمختص بالمحصورات الاربع كما توهم من ظاهر قول المصنف بل كما يجرى فيها، يجرى فى المهملات والشخصيات فاشتراط المصنف الاختلاف فى الكم ليس بمطلق بل مقيد بحال كونه بين المحصورتين.
It is answered that the consideration in all judgments is only to the concept of the proposition, and when the concept of the two particular propositions is observed—which is affirmation of some individuals and negation of some—they do not contradict. As for specifying the subject, it is a matter outside the concept. How so? The essence of the subject in the universal is all individuals, and in the particular is some of them, while there is contradiction between them. This. Then he said: 'if they were quantified' as an indication that contradiction is not restricted to the four quantified propositions, as might be imagined from the apparent meaning of the author's statement, but rather, just as it occurs in them, it occurs in indefinite and personal propositions. So the author's condition of difference in quantity is not absolute but restricted to the case of its being between two quantified propositions.
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This passage is a commentary expanding on the condition of difference in quantity for contradiction. It begins by answering an objection: why doesn't difference in quantity always apply? The answer is that the concept of a particular proposition (positive to some, negative to some) does not contradict another particular because their subjects differ in reference, but the essence of the subject differs between universal and particular (all vs. some), so contradiction exists. Then the commentator clarifies that the author's phrase 'if they were quantified' indicates that contradiction is not exclusive to quantified propositions; it also applies to indefinite and personal propositions. Therefore, the requirement of differing in quantity is not absolute but conditional on both propositions being quantified. This guards against the misunderstanding that contradiction only exists between quantified propositions.

مهملات

Reduction of Eight Unities to Two: Critique
Later scholars reduce eight unities to two

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the later reduction of the eight unities to two and evaluate the objection that the assignment is arbitrary.

Core Idea
Reducing unities to subject and predicate is useful but the allocation is not fixed.

Earlier logicians listed eight conditions for contradiction. Later scholars streamlined them to two: subject and predicate. But how should the other six be assigned? This passage presents a critique that any fixed assignment is arbitrary, and a defense that some associations are more natural.

Guided Path
1
Recall the eight unities
Review the eight conditions for genuine contradiction: subject, predicate, condition, part/whole, time, place, relation, potentiality/actuality.
2
Identify the reduction
Later scholars reduced them to two: unity of subject and unity of predicate. They assigned condition, part/whole to subject; the rest to predicate.
This is the target of the critique.
3
Analyze the objection
The objection says the assignment is arbitrary because if you convert a proposition (swap subject and predicate), the assignments would need to switch, showing no fixed relation.
The objection claims the reduction should not specify which belong to which.
4
Evaluate the defense
The author concedes the objection but notes that the original assignment is based on what is 'more apparent'—some unities naturally fit subject (condition, part/whole) and others predicate (time, place, etc.).
This defense appeals to conventional usage, not necessity.
5
Form your position
Decide whether the reduction without fixed assignment is better, or whether the natural fit justification suffices for logical practice.
Consider the role of convention in defining logical terms.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال الشيخ عبد الرحيم (ره) في تحقيق المقام ما هذا الفظه : اعلم : ان هذه الوحدات الثمانية ذكرها المتقدمون و ردها المتأخرون الى وحدتين وحدة الموضوع و وحدة المحمول، بان اندرجوا وحدة الشرط والجزء والكل في وحدة الموضوع و البواقي في وحدة المحمول. واعترض عليهم بان جعل بعض الوحدات راجعة الى وحدة الموضوع و بعضها الى وحدة المحمول تحكم، فان القضية اذا عكست انعكس ،الامر، فالأولى القول برجوع جميع الوحدات الى وحدة الموضوع و المحمول من غير تعيين بعضها للبعض وهذا الاعتراض حق الا ان المخصص كانه رعى ما هو الظاهر كما اشار اليه بعض المحققين من ان رجوع وحدة الشرط والجزء و الكل الى وحدة الموضوع و رجوع البواقي الى وحدة المحمول ،اظهر لان اعتبار الشرط والجزء والكل فى الموضوع و اعتبار الزمان والمكان والاضافة والقوة و الفعل في المحمول انسب.
And Shaykh Abd al-Rahim (may God have mercy on him) said in verifying the place [what follows]: Know that these eight unities were mentioned by the earlier scholars, and the later scholars reduced them to two unities: unity of subject and unity of predicate, by including the unity of condition, part, and whole under unity of subject, and the rest under unity of predicate. And an objection was raised against them: that assigning some unities to return to unity of subject and some to unity of predicate is arbitrary, because if the proposition is converted, the matter is reversed. So it is better to say that all the unities return to unity of subject and predicate without specifying some for one and some for the other. And this objection is true, except that the author (al-Mukhaṣṣiṣ?) seems to have observed what is apparent, as indicated by some investigators, that the return of unity of condition, part, and whole to unity of subject, and the return of the rest to unity of predicate, is more apparent, because considering condition, part, and whole in the subject, and considering time, place, relation, potentiality, and actuality in the predicate, is more appropriate.
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage presents a later scholarly refinement of the eight unities. Shaykh Abd al-Rahim explains that later logicians reduced the eight to just two: unity of subject and unity of predicate. They subsumed condition, whole/part under subject, and the rest under predicate. However, an objection is raised: this assignment is arbitrary because if you convert a proposition (change order), the assignment flips. The preferred view is to say all eight reduce to subject and predicate without specifying which goes where. The commentator notes that the objection is valid, but the original reduction is based on what is more apparent: condition, part, and whole are more naturally associated with the subject, while time, place, relation, potentiality, and actuality are more naturally associated with the predicate. This is a critical refinement of the traditional doctrine.

Key Terms
وحدات ثمانية
وحدة الموضوع
وحدة المحمول
تحكم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main objection against reducing the eight unities to two by assigning specific ones to subject and predicate?
A) The reduction is impossible because all eight are needed.
B) The assignment is arbitrary; if you convert the proposition, the assignment changes.
C) The later scholars misunderstood the ancient texts.
D) The reduction only works for affirmative propositions.

Key Takeaway
The eight unities can be reduced to subject and predicate, but any specific grouping is conventional, not necessary.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Take a proposition like 'al-ʿālamu ḥādithun' (the world is temporally originated). Convert it to 'ḥādithun huwa al-ʿālamu'. Explain how the reduction of unities applies differently after conversion, and argue whether the fixed assignment is justified.
?
Construct a pair of propositions that seem contradictory but fail due to a missing unity. Then reduce the check to just subject and predicate unities, showing the simplification.

The Eight Conditions for Contradiction
List of eight conditions for contradiction with examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which of the eight conditions is violated in a given pair of propositions.

Core Idea
A contradiction requires more than just opposite truth values; it demands unity across eight dimensions.

In this passage, the author lists eight conditions that must be met for two propositions to be truly contradictory. These go beyond just having opposite truth values – they ensure that the contradiction is genuine and not just apparent. Each condition is illustrated with concrete examples from everyday reasoning. By internalizing these conditions, you will be able to spot false contradictions in debates and theological arguments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two propositions in the example.
Locate the two statements that are claimed to be non-contradictory. Note their subject and predicate terms.
The examples are given in the Arabic, e.g., 'Every human is an animal' and 'Some stone is not an animal'.
2
Check the condition being discussed.
The example is introduced to illustrate violation of one of the eight conditions. Identify which condition (subject, predicate, place, etc.) is varied.
For instance, in the pearl example, the place differs (sea vs. chest).
3
Verify that both propositions could be true together.
If the condition is violated, the author shows that both can be true (or both false). Confirm this by considering the scenario described.
The pearl in the sea is surrounded by water, but the same pearl in a chest is not. So both statements are true.
4
Apply the condition to a new pair.
Given a new pair of Islamic-science propositions, test each of the eight conditions to see if any is violated.
Use the provided examples as a template.

(۱۱) لا يخفى فى ايراد كلتا الضروريتين هنا و فى ايراد كلتا الممكنتين بعيد هذا كليتين، من التسامح والاولى ايراد احديهما في المقامين جزئية لثلايتوهم ان الكذب هنا والصدق هنالك لعله لعدم الاختلاف في الكيف فلا يثبت المطلوب. (عبد الرحيم)
(۱۲) قوله : و قد ضبطوا هذا الاتحاد في ضمن الاتحاد في امور ثمانية»: قالوا ان التناقض لا يتحقق ولا يتصور الا بعد تحقق هذه الامور الثمانية المذكورة في البيتين: الاول وحدة الموضوع فانه لو اختلف الموضوع فى القضيتين لم يتناقضا الجواز ان تصدقا معاً نحو: كل انسان حيوان وليس بعض الحجر بحيوان وان تكذبا كعكس ذلك . الثانى وحدة المحمول، اذ لا تتناقضان عند اختلافه الجواز صدقهما معاً نحو كل انسان حیوان و بعض الانسان ليس بحجر و كذبها معاً كعكس ذلك . الثالث: وحدة المكان اذلو اختلف المكان لم تتناقضا لانها قد تصدقان معاً نحو: كل لؤلؤ محاط بالماء فى البحر و ليس بعض اللؤلؤ محاطاً بالماء فى الصندوق و قد تكذبان معاً كعكس الرابع: وحدة الشرط : اذ لا تناقض عند اختلافه تصدقهما في قولنا كل جسم مفرق للبصر اى بشرط كونه ابيض وبعض الجسم ليس بمفرق:ای بشرط كونه اسود فكذبهها معاً في عكس ذلك. الخامس: وحدة الاضافة اذ لو لم تتحد الاضافة لم تتناقضا لصدقهما معاً كقولنا: كل والد ما معا تقولنا كل والد اب اى
بالنسبة الى ابنه وبعض الوالد ليس بأب أى بالنسبة الى ابناء الغير و كذبهها في عكس ذلك. السادس: وحدة الكل والجزء لعدم التناقض عند اختلاف الكل والجزء الصدقهما معاً كقولنا : كل
الرجال عورة اى بعضه، و بعض الرجال ليس بصورة اى كله وكذبهها معاً في عكس ذلك. السابع وحدة القوة و الفعل اذلو اختلفا فيهما لم تتناقضا لجواز ان تصدقا معاً كقولنا كل خمر مسكر فى الدن اى بالقوة وليس بعضه بمسكر فيه اى بالفعل و كذبها معاً في عكس ذلك . الثامن: وحدة الزمان لعدم التناقض عند اختلافه لانها قد تصدقان معاً كقولنا كل انسان قوى اى فى زمن الشباب وبعض الانسان ليس بقوى اى فى زمن الشيخوخة وقد تكذبان معاً كعكس ذلك. ثم اعلم ان كون الشروط ثمانية انما هو على ما ذكره القدماء... (میرزا محمد علی)
( وقال الشيخ عبد الرحيم (ره) في تحقيق المقام ما هذا الفظه ) : اعلم : ان هذه الوحدات الثمانية ذكرها المتقدمون و ردها المتأخرون الى وحدتين وحدة الموضوع و وحدة المحمول، بان اندرجوا وحدة الشرط والجزء والكل في وحدة الموضوع و البواقي في وحدة المحمول. واعترض عليهم بان جعل بعض الوحدات راجعة الى وحدة الموضوع و بعضها الى وحدة المحمول تحكم، فان القضية اذا عكست انعكس ،الامر، فالأولى القول برجوع جميع الوحدات الى وحدة الموضوع و المحمول من غير تعيين بعضها للبعض وهذا الاعتراض حق الا ان المخصص كانه رعى ما هو الظاهر كما اشار اليه بعض المحققين من ان رجوع وحدة الشرط والجزء و الكل الى وحدة الموضوع و رجوع البواقي الى وحدة المحمول ،اظهر لان اعتبار الشرط والجزء والكل فى الموضوع و اعتبار الزمان والمكان والاضافة والقوة و الفعل في المحمول انسب.

اما وجه انسبية اعتبار الشرط في الموضوع فهو ان المراد بالموضوع في قولنا الجسم مفرق للبصر هو الذات اعنى المصداق واتصافه بالبياض والسواد لا يحتاج الى ملاحظة امر اخر. واما اذا وقع في جانب المحمول الذي يراد به المفهوم، فاتصافه بهما يحتاج الى ملاحظة الذات لان هذين الأمرين لا يعارضان الا للذات وكذا الكلام فى الكل والجزء.
و اما وجه انسبية اعتبار البواق فى المحمول فهو ان هذه الأمور قيد للمفهوم و المحمول يراد به المفهوم فاذا وقعت في جانب المحمول لم يحتج في تقييده بها الى ملاحظة امر آخر و اذا وقعت في جانب الموضوع الذي يراد به الذات يحتاج فى تقييده بها الى ملاحظة ذلك المفهوم.
:
وادعى الفارابي : الاكتفاء بامور ثلاثة من هذه الثمانية وهي وحدة الموضوع و المحمول والزمان، لان العلم الضروري حاصل بان ثبوت المحمول الواحد المعين للموضوع الواحد المعين في زمان معين وانتقائه عنه في عين ذلك الزمان مما لا يصدقان معاً ولا يكذبان والا لما تبعه في ذلك، فادرج باقي الوحدات في وحدة الموضوع والمحمول.
قال المحقق الابهرى ما ذكروه لبيان اندراج وحدة المكان في وحدة المحمول فهو بعينه تقتضي اندراج وحدة الزمان في وحدة المحمول لانا اذا قلنا القمر منخسف وقت حيلولة الارض بينه وبين الشمس و القمر ليس بمنخسف وقت التربيع بين النيرين كان المحمولان متغايرين ضرورة تغاير الانحساف وقت الحيلولة للانخساف وقت التربيع فكان يجب ان لا يعتبر اتحاد الموضوع و المحمول. هذا كلامه والامركيا
ذكره.
والامام ايضاً صرح بذلك في كتاب الآيات والبينات الكبير حيث قال: ان اشتراط وحدة الزمان مندرجة تحت وحدة المحمول الا انهم انها اعتبروا وحدة الزمان بالاستقلال لان كنه الأمر في التناقض وحدة، فالتصريح بهما يوجب زيادة الموضوع والاطلاع على رعايتهما يجب رعايته فيه . وقد ينقل عن الفارابي انه ذكر في بعض تصانيفه انه يمكن رد الشرايط كلها الى شرط واحد وهو الاتحاد في النسبة الحكمية لان اختلاف احدما ذكرنا من الامور موجب لاختلاف النسبة الحكمية اما اذا كان الاختلاف في الموضوع فلان نسبة الشيء الى احد المتغايرين غير نسبته الى المغاير الاخر واما اذا كان فى المحمول فلان نسبة احد المتغايرين الى الشيء غير نسبة الآخر اليه و اما اذا كان فى الزمان فلان نسبته الى غيره في احد الزمانين غير نسبة ذلك الشيء الى ذلك الغير فى الزمان الآخر و هكذا الكلام في البواقي وجميع هذه المقدمات ظاهر واذا ثبت ان اختلاف احد الامور موجب لاختلاف النسبة الحكمية ينعكس بعكس النقيض الى ان اتحاد النسبة الحكمية موجب لاتحاد الامور واذا كان كذلك
فنقول :
المعتبر في صحة التناقض اتحاد النسبة على معنى ان السلب يجب ان يكون وارداً على عين النسبة التي بها الحكم في الموجبة وبذلك كفاية في المخصوصات والمحصورات.
نعم الواردنا ان تعتبر التفصيل المفيد لزيادة الوضوح جعلنا الشرايط فى المخصوصات ثلاثة اتحاد الطرفين واتحاد الزمان والاختلاف بالضرورة واللاضرورة وبالجملة بالجهة و في المحصورات هذه الثلاثة مع الاختلاف بالكمية .
It is not hidden that in bringing both necessary [propositions] here and both possible [propositions] there as universal is lenient, and it is better to bring one of them in both cases as particular so that one does not imagine that falsity here and truth there is perhaps due to no difference in quality, thus the required is not established. (Abd al-Rahim)
His saying: 'And they have recorded this unity within the unity in eight matters': They said that contradiction does not occur nor is conceived except after the realization of these eight matters mentioned in the two verses: First, unity of subject, for if the subject differs in the two propositions they are not contradictory, because it is possible that they are both true, like: 'Every human is an animal' and 'Some stone is not an animal', and both false like the opposite. Second, unity of predicate, for they are not contradictory when it differs, as it is possible they are both true, like: 'Every human is an animal' and 'Some human is not a stone', and both false like the opposite. Third, unity of place, for if place differs they are not contradictory, because they can be both true, like: 'Every pearl is surrounded by water in the sea' and 'Some pearl is not surrounded by water in the chest', and both false like the opposite. Fourth, unity of condition, for there is no contradiction when it differs, their truth in our saying: 'Every body is dispersive of sight, i.e. on condition of being white' and 'Some body is not dispersive, i.e. on condition of being black', and both false in the opposite. Fifth, unity of relation, for if relation is not unified they are not contradictory, due to their being both true like our saying: 'Every parent is a father?', i.e. in relation to his son, and 'Some parent is not a father', i.e. in relation to others' sons, and both false in the opposite. Sixth, unity of whole and part, for there is no contradiction when whole and part differ, their being both true like our saying: 'All of the man is a defect?', i.e. some of him, and 'Some man is not a defect', i.e. all of him, and both false in the opposite. Seventh, unity of potentiality and actuality, for if they differ in them they are not contradictory, due to possibility of their being both true like our saying: 'Every wine is intoxicating in the jar, i.e. potentially' and 'Some wine is not intoxicating in it, i.e. actually', and both false in the opposite. Eighth, unity of time, for there is no contradiction when it differs, because they can be both true like our saying: 'Every human is strong, i.e. in youth' and 'Some human is not strong, i.e. in old age', and both false like the opposite. Then know that the conditions being eight is according to what the ancients mentioned... (Mirza Muhammad Ali)
(And Shaykh Abd al-Rahim (may Allah have mercy on him) said in investigating the subject, the words are:) Know: that these eight unities were mentioned by the predecessors and the later scholars reduced them to two unities: unity of subject and unity of predicate, by incorporating unity of condition, part, and whole into unity of subject, and the rest into unity of predicate. And they were objected to: that assigning some unities to unity of subject and some to unity of predicate is arbitrary, for if the proposition is converted, the matter is reversed. So it is better to say that all unities revert to unity of subject and predicate without specifying some for some. And this objection is correct, except that the commentator seems to have considered what is apparent, as indicated by some investigators, that reverting unity of condition, part, and whole to unity of subject, and the rest to unity of predicate is more appropriate, because considering condition, part, and whole in the subject, and considering time, place, relation, potentiality, and actuality in the predicate is more fitting.
As for the reason for the appropriateness of considering condition in the subject: it is that what is meant by the subject in our saying 'the body is dispersive of sight' is the essence, i.e., the referent, and its being described by whiteness and blackness does not need to observe another matter. But if it occurs on the side of the predicate, which is meant as the concept, then its being described by them needs to observe the essence, because these two attributes only pertain to the essence. And likewise the discussion about whole and part.
As for the reason for the appropriateness of considering the remaining [unities] in the predicate: it is that these matters are restrictions on the concept, and the predicate is meant as the concept, so if they occur on the side of the predicate, there is no need in restricting it by them to observe another matter. And if they occur on the side of the subject, which is meant as the essence, there is a need in restricting it by them to observe that concept.
And al-Farabi claimed sufficiency with three matters from these eight: unity of subject, predicate, and time, because necessary knowledge is obtained that the affirmation of one determined predicate for one determined subject at a determined time, and its negation concerning it at that same time, cannot be both true nor both false, otherwise he would not have followed that. So he incorporated the remaining unities into unity of subject and predicate.
Al-Muhaqqiq al-Abhari said: What they mentioned to explain the incorporation of unity of place into unity of predicate, it itself requires the incorporation of unity of time into unity of predicate, because if we say: 'The moon is eclipsed at the time of the earth's interposition between it and the sun' and 'The moon is not eclipsed at the time of quadrature between the two lights', then the two predicates are different necessarily due to the difference between the eclipse at the time of interposition and the eclipse at the time of quadrature, so unity of subject and predicate should not be considered. This is his statement, and the matter is as he mentioned.
And the Imam also explicitly stated that in the book al-Ayat wa al-Bayinat al-Kabir, where he said: Indeed, the condition of unity of time is subsumed under unity of predicate, except that they considered unity of time independently because the core of the matter in contradiction is unity, so making them explicit necessitates increasing the subject and being aware of observing them, and observing them is required in it. And it is reported from al-Farabi that he mentioned in some of his works that all conditions can be reduced to one condition: unity in the predicative relation, because difference in any of the matters we mentioned necessitates difference in the predicative relation. If the difference is in the subject, then the relation of a thing to one of the two different things is not its relation to the other different thing. If the difference is in the predicate, then the relation of one of the two different things to the thing is not the relation of the other to it. If the difference is in time, then its relation to other in one time is not the relation of that thing to that other in another time. And likewise the discussion about the rest. All these premises are apparent. And if it is established that difference in one of the matters necessitates difference in the predicative relation, then by contrapositive it follows that unity of the predicative relation necessitates unity of the matters. And if that is so, we say: What is considered in validity of contradiction is unity of relation, meaning that the negation must come upon the very relation by which the judgment is made in the affirmative. And this suffices for indefinite [singular] and quantified propositions. Yes, it is better for us to consider the detailed [conditions] that benefit additional clarity, so we make the conditions for indefinite [singular] three: unity of the two ends, unity of time, and difference by necessity and non-necessity, in short by modality. And for quantified [propositions], these three along with difference by quantity.
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage extensively defines the conditions for logical contradiction (tanāquḍ) between two propositions. It begins by noting a leniency in using universal propositions in examples where particular would be more precise, then lists eight conditions that must be met for two propositions to be truly contradictory. These are: unity of subject, predicate, place, condition, relation, whole/part, potentiality/actuality, and time. Each condition is illustrated with an example from the natural world or everyday reasoning, showing that if the condition is not met, both propositions can be true together or false together, thus no contradiction. The commentary then discusses the later reduction of these eight to two (subject and predicate) by later logicians, with an objection that the assignment is arbitrary. It provides a defense: condition, part, and whole are more appropriately considered aspects of the subject, while the rest belong to the predicate, based on whether the term refers to essence (subject) or concept (predicate). Al-Farabi is cited as requiring only three: subject, predicate, and time, because necessary knowledge tells us that a proposition and its negation cannot both be true or false at the same time for the same subject and predicate. Al-Abhari then argues that if place is subsumed under predicate, then time should also be subsumed, because different times yield different predicates. The Imam (al-Razi) agrees but notes that time was mentioned independently for clarity. Finally, al-Farabi is reported to have reduced all to a single condition: unity of the predicative relation. The essence of contradiction is that the negation negates the very relational judgment of the affirmation. This single condition suffices, but for clarity, the conventional division into three for indefinite (singular) propositions (unity of subject and predicate, unity of time, and difference in modality) and four for quantified (adding difference in quantity) is maintained.

Checkpoint
Which condition is violated in the pair: 'Every person is praying in the mosque' and 'Some person is not praying in the house'?
A) Unity of subject
B) Unity of predicate
C) Unity of place
D) Unity of time

Key Takeaway
Contradiction requires unity across eight conditions; if any one condition is not met, both propositions can be true together.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the pair: 'Every act of worship requires intention (niyya)' and 'Some act of worship does not require intention (e.g., removing harm)'. Identify which condition(s) might be violated if both are true, using the eight conditions.
?
Take the example from usul al-fiqh: 'Zakat is obligatory on wealth' and 'Zakat is not obligatory on certain wealth (e.g., debts)'. Check if the conditions allow both to be true.

Immediate Inference
intermediate
10 min
Reduction of Conditions to Two: Subject and Predicate
Reduction of eight conditions to two and the objection of arbitrariness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how later logicians reduced the eight conditions to two and evaluate the objection about arbitrariness.

Core Idea
Eight conditions reduce to two by noting whether the variation affects the referent (subject) or the concept (predicate).

The passage then discusses how later logicians reduced the eight conditions to just two: unity of subject and unity of predicate. They argued that conditions like place, time, relation, potentiality, and actuality pertain to the predicate, while condition, whole, and part pertain to the subject. However, this assignment was criticized as arbitrary because converting the proposition could reverse the roles. The commentator defends the assignment based on whether the term refers to essence (subject) or concept (predicate).

Guided Path
1
Understand the reduction scheme.
Later logicians subsumed condition, part, and whole under unity of subject; the remaining five (place, time, relation, potentiality, actuality) under unity of predicate.
This is based on the nature of the subject as essence/referent and predicate as concept.
2
Grasp the objection.
Critics said the assignment is arbitrary because if you convert the proposition (e.g., change the subject to predicate), the condition that was in the subject might move to the predicate, so there is no fixed correspondence.
For example, 'Every human is an animal' converted to 'Some animal is human' switches subject and predicate.
3
Analyze the defense.
The commentator argues that it is more appropriate (azhar) to assign condition, whole, part to the subject because these qualify the essence directly, while the rest qualify the concept. This is based on whether the term is taken as referent or meaning.
White/black as conditions affect the subject's essence; time/place as predicates affect the concept.
4
Apply the distinction.
Given a new example, decide whether a given variation pertains to the subject side or predicate side according to this scheme.
Consider if the variation changes the referent itself or just the attribute.
