(۱۲) قوله : و قد ضبطوا هذا الاتحاد في ضمن الاتحاد في امور ثمانية»: قالوا ان التناقض لا يتحقق ولا يتصور الا بعد تحقق هذه الامور الثمانية المذكورة في البيتين: الاول وحدة الموضوع فانه لو اختلف الموضوع فى القضيتين لم يتناقضا الجواز ان تصدقا معاً نحو: كل انسان حيوان وليس بعض الحجر بحيوان وان تكذبا كعكس ذلك . الثانى وحدة المحمول، اذ لا تتناقضان عند اختلافه الجواز صدقهما معاً نحو كل انسان حیوان و بعض الانسان ليس بحجر و كذبها معاً كعكس ذلك . الثالث: وحدة المكان اذلو اختلف المكان لم تتناقضا لانها قد تصدقان معاً نحو: كل لؤلؤ محاط بالماء فى البحر و ليس بعض اللؤلؤ محاطاً بالماء فى الصندوق و قد تكذبان معاً كعكس الرابع: وحدة الشرط : اذ لا تناقض عند اختلافه تصدقهما في قولنا كل جسم مفرق للبصر اى بشرط كونه ابيض وبعض الجسم ليس بمفرق:ای بشرط كونه اسود فكذبهها معاً في عكس ذلك. الخامس: وحدة الاضافة اذ لو لم تتحد الاضافة لم تتناقضا لصدقهما معاً كقولنا: كل والد ما معا تقولنا كل والد اب اى
بالنسبة الى ابنه وبعض الوالد ليس بأب أى بالنسبة الى ابناء الغير و كذبهها في عكس ذلك. السادس: وحدة الكل والجزء لعدم التناقض عند اختلاف الكل والجزء الصدقهما معاً كقولنا : كل
الرجال عورة اى بعضه، و بعض الرجال ليس بصورة اى كله وكذبهها معاً في عكس ذلك. السابع وحدة القوة و الفعل اذلو اختلفا فيهما لم تتناقضا لجواز ان تصدقا معاً كقولنا كل خمر مسكر فى الدن اى بالقوة وليس بعضه بمسكر فيه اى بالفعل و كذبها معاً في عكس ذلك . الثامن: وحدة الزمان لعدم التناقض عند اختلافه لانها قد تصدقان معاً كقولنا كل انسان قوى اى فى زمن الشباب وبعض الانسان ليس بقوى اى فى زمن الشيخوخة وقد تكذبان معاً كعكس ذلك. ثم اعلم ان كون الشروط ثمانية انما هو على ما ذكره القدماء... (میرزا محمد علی)
( وقال الشيخ عبد الرحيم (ره) في تحقيق المقام ما هذا الفظه ) : اعلم : ان هذه الوحدات الثمانية ذكرها المتقدمون و ردها المتأخرون الى وحدتين وحدة الموضوع و وحدة المحمول، بان اندرجوا وحدة الشرط والجزء والكل في وحدة الموضوع و البواقي في وحدة المحمول. واعترض عليهم بان جعل بعض الوحدات راجعة الى وحدة الموضوع و بعضها الى وحدة المحمول تحكم، فان القضية اذا عكست انعكس ،الامر، فالأولى القول برجوع جميع الوحدات الى وحدة الموضوع و المحمول من غير تعيين بعضها للبعض وهذا الاعتراض حق الا ان المخصص كانه رعى ما هو الظاهر كما اشار اليه بعض المحققين من ان رجوع وحدة الشرط والجزء و الكل الى وحدة الموضوع و رجوع البواقي الى وحدة المحمول ،اظهر لان اعتبار الشرط والجزء والكل فى الموضوع و اعتبار الزمان والمكان والاضافة والقوة و الفعل في المحمول انسب.

اما وجه انسبية اعتبار الشرط في الموضوع فهو ان المراد بالموضوع في قولنا الجسم مفرق للبصر هو الذات اعنى المصداق واتصافه بالبياض والسواد لا يحتاج الى ملاحظة امر اخر. واما اذا وقع في جانب المحمول الذي يراد به المفهوم، فاتصافه بهما يحتاج الى ملاحظة الذات لان هذين الأمرين لا يعارضان الا للذات وكذا الكلام فى الكل والجزء.
و اما وجه انسبية اعتبار البواق فى المحمول فهو ان هذه الأمور قيد للمفهوم و المحمول يراد به المفهوم فاذا وقعت في جانب المحمول لم يحتج في تقييده بها الى ملاحظة امر آخر و اذا وقعت في جانب الموضوع الذي يراد به الذات يحتاج فى تقييده بها الى ملاحظة ذلك المفهوم.
:
وادعى الفارابي : الاكتفاء بامور ثلاثة من هذه الثمانية وهي وحدة الموضوع و المحمول والزمان، لان العلم الضروري حاصل بان ثبوت المحمول الواحد المعين للموضوع الواحد المعين في زمان معين وانتقائه عنه في عين ذلك الزمان مما لا يصدقان معاً ولا يكذبان والا لما تبعه في ذلك، فادرج باقي الوحدات في وحدة الموضوع والمحمول.
قال المحقق الابهرى ما ذكروه لبيان اندراج وحدة المكان في وحدة المحمول فهو بعينه تقتضي اندراج وحدة الزمان في وحدة المحمول لانا اذا قلنا القمر منخسف وقت حيلولة الارض بينه وبين الشمس و القمر ليس بمنخسف وقت التربيع بين النيرين كان المحمولان متغايرين ضرورة تغاير الانحساف وقت الحيلولة للانخساف وقت التربيع فكان يجب ان لا يعتبر اتحاد الموضوع و المحمول. هذا كلامه والامركيا
ذكره.
والامام ايضاً صرح بذلك في كتاب الآيات والبينات الكبير حيث قال: ان اشتراط وحدة الزمان مندرجة تحت وحدة المحمول الا انهم انها اعتبروا وحدة الزمان بالاستقلال لان كنه الأمر في التناقض وحدة، فالتصريح بهما يوجب زيادة الموضوع والاطلاع على رعايتهما يجب رعايته فيه . وقد ينقل عن الفارابي انه ذكر في بعض تصانيفه انه يمكن رد الشرايط كلها الى شرط واحد وهو الاتحاد في النسبة الحكمية لان اختلاف احدما ذكرنا من الامور موجب لاختلاف النسبة الحكمية اما اذا كان الاختلاف في الموضوع فلان نسبة الشيء الى احد المتغايرين غير نسبته الى المغاير الاخر واما اذا كان فى المحمول فلان نسبة احد المتغايرين الى الشيء غير نسبة الآخر اليه و اما اذا كان فى الزمان فلان نسبته الى غيره في احد الزمانين غير نسبة ذلك الشيء الى ذلك الغير فى الزمان الآخر و هكذا الكلام في البواقي وجميع هذه المقدمات ظاهر واذا ثبت ان اختلاف احد الامور موجب لاختلاف النسبة الحكمية ينعكس بعكس النقيض الى ان اتحاد النسبة الحكمية موجب لاتحاد الامور واذا كان كذلك
فنقول :
المعتبر في صحة التناقض اتحاد النسبة على معنى ان السلب يجب ان يكون وارداً على عين النسبة التي بها الحكم في الموجبة وبذلك كفاية في المخصوصات والمحصورات.
نعم الواردنا ان تعتبر التفصيل المفيد لزيادة الوضوح جعلنا الشرايط فى المخصوصات ثلاثة اتحاد الطرفين واتحاد الزمان والاختلاف بالضرورة واللاضرورة وبالجملة بالجهة و في المحصورات هذه الثلاثة مع الاختلاف بالكمية .
It is not hidden that in bringing both necessary [propositions] here and both possible [propositions] there as universal is lenient, and it is better to bring one of them in both cases as particular so that one does not imagine that falsity here and truth there is perhaps due to no difference in quality, thus the required is not established. (Abd al-Rahim)
His saying: 'And they have recorded this unity within the unity in eight matters': They said that contradiction does not occur nor is conceived except after the realization of these eight matters mentioned in the two verses: First, unity of subject, for if the subject differs in the two propositions they are not contradictory, because it is possible that they are both true, like: 'Every human is an animal' and 'Some stone is not an animal', and both false like the opposite. Second, unity of predicate, for they are not contradictory when it differs, as it is possible they are both true, like: 'Every human is an animal' and 'Some human is not a stone', and both false like the opposite. Third, unity of place, for if place differs they are not contradictory, because they can be both true, like: 'Every pearl is surrounded by water in the sea' and 'Some pearl is not surrounded by water in the chest', and both false like the opposite. Fourth, unity of condition, for there is no contradiction when it differs, their truth in our saying: 'Every body is dispersive of sight, i.e. on condition of being white' and 'Some body is not dispersive, i.e. on condition of being black', and both false in the opposite. Fifth, unity of relation, for if relation is not unified they are not contradictory, due to their being both true like our saying: 'Every parent is a father?', i.e. in relation to his son, and 'Some parent is not a father', i.e. in relation to others' sons, and both false in the opposite. Sixth, unity of whole and part, for there is no contradiction when whole and part differ, their being both true like our saying: 'All of the man is a defect?', i.e. some of him, and 'Some man is not a defect', i.e. all of him, and both false in the opposite. Seventh, unity of potentiality and actuality, for if they differ in them they are not contradictory, due to possibility of their being both true like our saying: 'Every wine is intoxicating in the jar, i.e. potentially' and 'Some wine is not intoxicating in it, i.e. actually', and both false in the opposite. Eighth, unity of time, for there is no contradiction when it differs, because they can be both true like our saying: 'Every human is strong, i.e. in youth' and 'Some human is not strong, i.e. in old age', and both false like the opposite. Then know that the conditions being eight is according to what the ancients mentioned... (Mirza Muhammad Ali)
(And Shaykh Abd al-Rahim (may Allah have mercy on him) said in investigating the subject, the words are:) Know: that these eight unities were mentioned by the predecessors and the later scholars reduced them to two unities: unity of subject and unity of predicate, by incorporating unity of condition, part, and whole into unity of subject, and the rest into unity of predicate. And they were objected to: that assigning some unities to unity of subject and some to unity of predicate is arbitrary, for if the proposition is converted, the matter is reversed. So it is better to say that all unities revert to unity of subject and predicate without specifying some for some. And this objection is correct, except that the commentator seems to have considered what is apparent, as indicated by some investigators, that reverting unity of condition, part, and whole to unity of subject, and the rest to unity of predicate is more appropriate, because considering condition, part, and whole in the subject, and considering time, place, relation, potentiality, and actuality in the predicate is more fitting.
As for the reason for the appropriateness of considering condition in the subject: it is that what is meant by the subject in our saying 'the body is dispersive of sight' is the essence, i.e., the referent, and its being described by whiteness and blackness does not need to observe another matter. But if it occurs on the side of the predicate, which is meant as the concept, then its being described by them needs to observe the essence, because these two attributes only pertain to the essence. And likewise the discussion about whole and part.
As for the reason for the appropriateness of considering the remaining [unities] in the predicate: it is that these matters are restrictions on the concept, and the predicate is meant as the concept, so if they occur on the side of the predicate, there is no need in restricting it by them to observe another matter. And if they occur on the side of the subject, which is meant as the essence, there is a need in restricting it by them to observe that concept.
And al-Farabi claimed sufficiency with three matters from these eight: unity of subject, predicate, and time, because necessary knowledge is obtained that the affirmation of one determined predicate for one determined subject at a determined time, and its negation concerning it at that same time, cannot be both true nor both false, otherwise he would not have followed that. So he incorporated the remaining unities into unity of subject and predicate.
Al-Muhaqqiq al-Abhari said: What they mentioned to explain the incorporation of unity of place into unity of predicate, it itself requires the incorporation of unity of time into unity of predicate, because if we say: 'The moon is eclipsed at the time of the earth's interposition between it and the sun' and 'The moon is not eclipsed at the time of quadrature between the two lights', then the two predicates are different necessarily due to the difference between the eclipse at the time of interposition and the eclipse at the time of quadrature, so unity of subject and predicate should not be considered. This is his statement, and the matter is as he mentioned.
And the Imam also explicitly stated that in the book al-Ayat wa al-Bayinat al-Kabir, where he said: Indeed, the condition of unity of time is subsumed under unity of predicate, except that they considered unity of time independently because the core of the matter in contradiction is unity, so making them explicit necessitates increasing the subject and being aware of observing them, and observing them is required in it. And it is reported from al-Farabi that he mentioned in some of his works that all conditions can be reduced to one condition: unity in the predicative relation, because difference in any of the matters we mentioned necessitates difference in the predicative relation. If the difference is in the subject, then the relation of a thing to one of the two different things is not its relation to the other different thing. If the difference is in the predicate, then the relation of one of the two different things to the thing is not the relation of the other to it. If the difference is in time, then its relation to other in one time is not the relation of that thing to that other in another time. And likewise the discussion about the rest. All these premises are apparent. And if it is established that difference in one of the matters necessitates difference in the predicative relation, then by contrapositive it follows that unity of the predicative relation necessitates unity of the matters. And if that is so, we say: What is considered in validity of contradiction is unity of relation, meaning that the negation must come upon the very relation by which the judgment is made in the affirmative. And this suffices for indefinite [singular] and quantified propositions. Yes, it is better for us to consider the detailed [conditions] that benefit additional clarity, so we make the conditions for indefinite [singular] three: unity of the two ends, unity of time, and difference by necessity and non-necessity, in short by modality. And for quantified [propositions], these three along with difference by quantity.
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage extensively defines the conditions for logical contradiction (tanāquḍ) between two propositions. It begins by noting a leniency in using universal propositions in examples where particular would be more precise, then lists eight conditions that must be met for two propositions to be truly contradictory. These are: unity of subject, predicate, place, condition, relation, whole/part, potentiality/actuality, and time. Each condition is illustrated with an example from the natural world or everyday reasoning, showing that if the condition is not met, both propositions can be true together or false together, thus no contradiction. The commentary then discusses the later reduction of these eight to two (subject and predicate) by later logicians, with an objection that the assignment is arbitrary. It provides a defense: condition, part, and whole are more appropriately considered aspects of the subject, while the rest belong to the predicate, based on whether the term refers to essence (subject) or concept (predicate). Al-Farabi is cited as requiring only three: subject, predicate, and time, because necessary knowledge tells us that a proposition and its negation cannot both be true or false at the same time for the same subject and predicate. Al-Abhari then argues that if place is subsumed under predicate, then time should also be subsumed, because different times yield different predicates. The Imam (al-Razi) agrees but notes that time was mentioned independently for clarity. Finally, al-Farabi is reported to have reduced all to a single condition: unity of the predicative relation. The essence of contradiction is that the negation negates the very relational judgment of the affirmation. This single condition suffices, but for clarity, the conventional division into three for indefinite (singular) propositions (unity of subject and predicate, unity of time, and difference in modality) and four for quantified (adding difference in quantity) is maintained.

Checkpoint
What is the main objection to the reduction of eight conditions to two?
A) The reduction is too complex.
B) The assignment of conditions to subject or predicate is arbitrary because converting the proposition can reverse roles.
C) The two conditions are insufficient to guarantee contradiction.
D) The reduction was not accepted by later logicians.

Key Takeaway
The eight conditions reduce to two (subject and predicate) but the assignment is defended as more appropriate based on the nature of subject as essence and predicate as concept.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Take the pair: 'Fasting is obligatory on every Muslim who is adult and sane' and 'Fasting is not obligatory on a Muslim who is insane'. Here the condition (sanity) varies. According to the reduction, does this variation pertain to the subject or predicate? Explain.
?
In a debate about whether 'Zakat is obligatory on wealth that reaches nisab' and 'Zakat is not obligatory on wealth that is less than nisab', identify which of the eight conditions is being varied and whether it falls under subject or predicate in the reduction scheme.

Immediate Inference
advanced
12 min
Al-Farabi's Reduction to One: The Predicative Relation
Reduction of all conditions to unity of predicative relation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the argument that all conditions reduce to unity of the predicative relation and apply it to specific examples.

Core Idea
All conditions for contradiction ultimately boil down to one: the negation must negate the exact same relational tie affirmed.

The passage culminates with al-Farabi's claim that all eight conditions can be reduced to a single condition: unity of the predicative relation (al-nisba al-ḥukmiyya). The logic is that any difference in subject, predicate, time, etc., results in a different relational tie between subject and predicate. By contrapositive, if the relational tie is the same, then all conditions are unified. This elegant reduction captures the essence of contradiction. The passage also discusses whether time is independent or subsumed under predicate, and al-Abhari's argument that time should likewise be subsumed.

Guided Path
1
Understand the concept of 'predicative relation'.
The predicative relation is the tie (nisba) between subject and predicate that is affirmed or denied. For example, in 'Zayd is standing', the relation is the is-ness or standing-ness attributed to Zayd.
It is not the subject or predicate themselves but the connection.
2
Follow the argument for reduction.
Al-Farabi argues: if any condition (subject, predicate, time, etc.) differs, then the relational tie differs. Therefore, if the relational tie is the same, all conditions must be the same. Contrapositively, unity of relation implies unity of all conditions.
This is an immediate inference (contrapositive) from 'difference in condition implies difference in relation' to 'unity of relation implies unity of condition'.
3
Examine the sub-discussion about time.
Al-Abhari notes that if place is subsumed under predicate (as earlier reduction had it), then time should also be subsumed because different times yield different predicates (e.g., 'eclipsed at time T1' vs 'not eclipsed at time T2'). The Imam (al-Razi) agrees but says time was mentioned independently for clarity.
Al-Farabi himself kept time as a separate condition in his three-condition list.
4
Apply the single-condition test.
Given a pair of propositions, check if the negation negates the exact same relational tie as the affirmation. If yes, it is a genuine contradiction; otherwise not.
For example, 'Zayd is writing' and 'Zayd is not writing' have the same relational tie (writing attributed to Zayd). But 'Zayd is writing' and 'Amr is not writing' have different subjects, hence different relations.

(۱۱) لا يخفى فى ايراد كلتا الضروريتين هنا و فى ايراد كلتا الممكنتين بعيد هذا كليتين، من التسامح والاولى ايراد احديهما في المقامين جزئية لثلايتوهم ان الكذب هنا والصدق هنالك لعله لعدم الاختلاف في الكيف فلا يثبت المطلوب. (عبد الرحيم)

الرجال عورة اى بعضه، و بعض الرجال ليس بصورة اى كله وكذبهها معاً في عكس ذلك. السابع وحدة القوة و الفعل اذلو اختلفا فيهما لم تتناقضا لجواز ان تصدقا معاً كقولنا كل خمر مسكر فى الدن اى بالقوة وليس بعضه بمسكر فيه اى بالفعل و كذبها معاً في عكس ذلك . الثامن: وحدة الزمان لعدم التناقض عند اختلافه لانها قد تصدقان معاً كقولنا كل انسان قوى اى فى زمن الشباب وبعض الانسان ليس بقوى اى فى زمن الشيخوخة وقد تكذبان معاً كعكس ذلك. ثم اعلم ان كون الشروط ثمانية انما هو على ما ذكره القدماء... ( وقال الشيخ عبد الرحيم (ره) في تحقيق المقام ما هذا الفظه ) : اعلم : ان هذه الوحدات الثمانية ذكرها المتقدمون و ردها المتأخرون الى وحدتين وحدة الموضوع و وحدة المحمول، بان اندرجوا وحدة الشرط والجزء والكل في وحدة الموضوع و البواقي في وحدة المحمول. واعترض عليهم بان جعل بعض الوحدات راجعة الى وحدة الموضوع و بعضها الى وحدة المحمول تحكم، فان القضية اذا عكست انعكس ،الامر، فالأولى القول برجوع جميع الوحدات الى وحدة الموضوع و المحمول من غير تعيين بعضها للبعض وهذا الاعتراض حق الا ان المخصص كانه رعى ما هو الظاهر كما اشار اليه بعض المحققين من ان رجوع وحدة الشرط والجزء و الكل الى وحدة الموضوع و رجوع البواقي الى وحدة المحمول ،اظهر لان اعتبار الشرط والجزء والكل فى الموضوع و اعتبار الزمان والمكان والاضافة والقوة و الفعل في المحمول انسب.

اما وجه انسبية اعتبار الشرط في الموضوع فهو ان المراد بالموضوع في قولنا الجسم مفرق للبصر هو الذات اعنى المصداق واتصافه بالبياض والسواد لا يحتاج الى ملاحظة امر اخر. واما اذا وقع في جانب المحمول الذي يراد به المفهوم، فاتصافه بهما يحتاج الى ملاحظة الذات لان هذين الأمرين لا يعارضان الا للذات وكذا الكلام فى الكل والجزء.
و اما وجه انسبية اعتبار البواق فى المحمول فهو ان هذه الأمور قيد للمفهوم و المحمول يراد به المفهوم فاذا وقعت في جانب المحمول لم يحتج في تقييده بها الى ملاحظة امر آخر و اذا وقعت في جانب الموضوع الذي يراد به الذات يحتاج فى تقييده بها الى ملاحظة ذلك المفهوم.
:
وادعى الفارابي : الاكتفاء بامور ثلاثة من هذه الثمانية وهي وحدة الموضوع و المحمول والزمان، لان العلم الضروري حاصل بان ثبوت المحمول الواحد المعين للموضوع الواحد المعين في زمان معين وانتقائه عنه في عين ذلك الزمان مما لا يصدقان معاً ولا يكذبان والا لما تبعه في ذلك، فادرج باقي الوحدات في وحدة الموضوع والمحمول.
قال المحقق الابهرى ما ذكروه لبيان اندراج وحدة المكان في وحدة المحمول فهو بعينه تقتضي اندراج وحدة الزمان في وحدة المحمول لانا اذا قلنا القمر منخسف وقت حيلولة الارض بينه وبين الشمس و القمر ليس بمنخسف وقت التربيع بين النيرين كان المحمولان متغايرين ضرورة تغاير الانحساف وقت الحيلولة للانخساف وقت التربيع فكان يجب ان لا يعتبر اتحاد الموضوع و المحمول. هذا كلامه والامركيا
ذكره.
والامام ايضاً صرح بذلك في كتاب الآيات والبينات الكبير حيث قال: ان اشتراط وحدة الزمان مندرجة تحت وحدة المحمول الا انهم انها اعتبروا وحدة الزمان بالاستقلال لان كنه الأمر في التناقض وحدة، فالتصريح بهما يوجب زيادة الموضوع والاطلاع على رعايتهما يجب رعايته فيه . وقد ينقل عن الفارابي انه ذكر في بعض تصانيفه انه يمكن رد الشرايط كلها الى شرط واحد وهو الاتحاد في النسبة الحكمية لان اختلاف احدما ذكرنا من الامور موجب لاختلاف النسبة الحكمية اما اذا كان الاختلاف في الموضوع فلان نسبة الشيء الى احد المتغايرين غير نسبته الى المغاير الاخر واما اذا كان فى المحمول فلان نسبة احد المتغايرين الى الشيء غير نسبة الآخر اليه و اما اذا كان فى الزمان فلان نسبته الى غيره في احد الزمانين غير نسبة ذلك الشيء الى ذلك الغير فى الزمان الآخر و هكذا الكلام في البواقي وجميع هذه المقدمات ظاهر واذا ثبت ان اختلاف احد الامور موجب لاختلاف النسبة الحكمية ينعكس بعكس النقيض الى ان اتحاد النسبة الحكمية موجب لاتحاد الامور واذا كان كذلك
فنقول :
المعتبر في صحة التناقض اتحاد النسبة على معنى ان السلب يجب ان يكون وارداً على عين النسبة التي بها الحكم في الموجبة وبذلك كفاية في المخصوصات والمحصورات.
نعم الواردنا ان تعتبر التفصيل المفيد لزيادة الوضوح جعلنا الشرايط فى المخصوصات ثلاثة اتحاد الطرفين واتحاد الزمان والاختلاف بالضرورة واللاضرورة وبالجملة بالجهة و في المحصورات هذه الثلاثة مع الاختلاف بالكمية .
It is not hidden that in bringing both necessary [propositions] here and both possible [propositions] there as universal is lenient, and it is better to bring one of them in both cases as particular so that one does not imagine that falsity here and truth there is perhaps due to no difference in quality, thus the required is not established. (Abd al-Rahim)
His saying: 'And they have recorded this unity within the unity in eight matters': They said that contradiction does not occur nor is conceived except after the realization of these eight matters mentioned in the two verses: First, unity of subject, for if the subject differs in the two propositions they are not contradictory, because it is possible that they are both true, like: 'Every human is an animal' and 'Some stone is not an animal', and both false like the opposite. Second, unity of predicate, for they are not contradictory when it differs, as it is possible they are both true, like: 'Every human is an animal' and 'Some human is not a stone', and both false like the opposite. Third, unity of place, for if place differs they are not contradictory, because they can be both true, like: 'Every pearl is surrounded by water in the sea' and 'Some pearl is not surrounded by water in the chest', and both false like the opposite. Fourth, unity of condition, for there is no contradiction when it differs, their truth in our saying: 'Every body is dispersive of sight, i.e. on condition of being white' and 'Some body is not dispersive, i.e. on condition of being black', and both false in the opposite. Fifth, unity of relation, for if relation is not unified they are not contradictory, due to their being both true like our saying: 'Every parent is a father?', i.e. in relation to his son, and 'Some parent is not a father', i.e. in relation to others' sons, and both false in the opposite. Sixth, unity of whole and part, for there is no contradiction when whole and part differ, their being both true like our saying: 'All of the man is a defect?', i.e. some of him, and 'Some man is not a defect', i.e. all of him, and both false in the opposite. Seventh, unity of potentiality and actuality, for if they differ in them they are not contradictory, due to possibility of their being both true like our saying: 'Every wine is intoxicating in the jar, i.e. potentially' and 'Some wine is not intoxicating in it, i.e. actually', and both false in the opposite. Eighth, unity of time, for there is no contradiction when it differs, because they can be both true like our saying: 'Every human is strong, i.e. in youth' and 'Some human is not strong, i.e. in old age', and both false like the opposite. Then know that the conditions being eight is according to what the ancients mentioned... (Mirza Muhammad Ali)
(And Shaykh Abd al-Rahim (may Allah have mercy on him) said in investigating the subject, the words are:) Know: that these eight unities were mentioned by the predecessors and the later scholars reduced them to two unities: unity of subject and unity of predicate, by incorporating unity of condition, part, and whole into unity of subject, and the rest into unity of predicate. And they were objected to: that assigning some unities to unity of subject and some to unity of predicate is arbitrary, for if the proposition is converted, the matter is reversed. So it is better to say that all unities revert to unity of subject and predicate without specifying some for some. And this objection is correct, except that the commentator seems to have considered what is apparent, as indicated by some investigators, that reverting unity of condition, part, and whole to unity of subject, and the rest to unity of predicate is more appropriate, because considering condition, part, and whole in the subject, and considering time, place, relation, potentiality, and actuality in the predicate is more fitting.
As for the reason for the appropriateness of considering condition in the subject: it is that what is meant by the subject in our saying 'the body is dispersive of sight' is the essence, i.e., the referent, and its being described by whiteness and blackness does not need to observe another matter. But if it occurs on the side of the predicate, which is meant as the concept, then its being described by them needs to observe the essence, because these two attributes only pertain to the essence. And likewise the discussion about whole and part.
As for the reason for the appropriateness of considering the remaining [unities] in the predicate: it is that these matters are restrictions on the concept, and the predicate is meant as the concept, so if they occur on the side of the predicate, there is no need in restricting it by them to observe another matter. And if they occur on the side of the subject, which is meant as the essence, there is a need in restricting it by them to observe that concept.
And al-Farabi claimed sufficiency with three matters from these eight: unity of subject, predicate, and time, because necessary knowledge is obtained that the affirmation of one determined predicate for one determined subject at a determined time, and its negation concerning it at that same time, cannot be both true nor both false, otherwise he would not have followed that. So he incorporated the remaining unities into unity of subject and predicate.
Al-Muhaqqiq al-Abhari said: What they mentioned to explain the incorporation of unity of place into unity of predicate, it itself requires the incorporation of unity of time into unity of predicate, because if we say: 'The moon is eclipsed at the time of the earth's interposition between it and the sun' and 'The moon is not eclipsed at the time of quadrature between the two lights', then the two predicates are different necessarily due to the difference between the eclipse at the time of interposition and the eclipse at the time of quadrature, so unity of subject and predicate should not be considered. This is his statement, and the matter is as he mentioned.
And the Imam also explicitly stated that in the book al-Ayat wa al-Bayinat al-Kabir, where he said: Indeed, the condition of unity of time is subsumed under unity of predicate, except that they considered unity of time independently because the core of the matter in contradiction is unity, so making them explicit necessitates increasing the subject and being aware of observing them, and observing them is required in it. And it is reported from al-Farabi that he mentioned in some of his works that all conditions can be reduced to one condition: unity in the predicative relation, because difference in any of the matters we mentioned necessitates difference in the predicative relation. If the difference is in the subject, then the relation of a thing to one of the two different things is not its relation to the other different thing. If the difference is in the predicate, then the relation of one of the two different things to the thing is not the relation of the other to it. If the difference is in time, then its relation to other in one time is not the relation of that thing to that other in another time. And likewise the discussion about the rest. All these premises are apparent. And if it is established that difference in one of the matters necessitates difference in the predicative relation, then by contrapositive it follows that unity of the predicative relation necessitates unity of the matters. And if that is so, we say: What is considered in validity of contradiction is unity of relation, meaning that the negation must come upon the very relation by which the judgment is made in the affirmative. And this suffices for indefinite [singular] and quantified propositions. Yes, it is better for us to consider the detailed [conditions] that benefit additional clarity, so we make the conditions for indefinite [singular] three: unity of the two ends, unity of time, and difference by necessity and non-necessity, in short by modality. And for quantified [propositions], these three along with difference by quantity.
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage extensively defines the conditions for logical contradiction (tanāquḍ) between two propositions. It begins by noting a leniency in using universal propositions in examples where particular would be more precise, then lists eight conditions that must be met for two propositions to be truly contradictory. These are: unity of subject, predicate, place, condition, relation, whole/part, potentiality/actuality, and time. Each condition is illustrated with an example from the natural world or everyday reasoning, showing that if the condition is not met, both propositions can be true together or false together, thus no contradiction. The commentary then discusses the later reduction of these eight to two (subject and predicate) by later logicians, with an objection that the assignment is arbitrary. It provides a defense: condition, part, and whole are more appropriately considered aspects of the subject, while the rest belong to the predicate, based on whether the term refers to essence (subject) or concept (predicate). Al-Farabi is cited as requiring only three: subject, predicate, and time, because necessary knowledge tells us that a proposition and its negation cannot both be true or false at the same time for the same subject and predicate. Al-Abhari then argues that if place is subsumed under predicate, then time should also be subsumed, because different times yield different predicates. The Imam (al-Razi) agrees but notes that time was mentioned independently for clarity. Finally, al-Farabi is reported to have reduced all to a single condition: unity of the predicative relation. The essence of contradiction is that the negation negates the very relational judgment of the affirmation. This single condition suffices, but for clarity, the conventional division into three for indefinite (singular) propositions (unity of subject and predicate, unity of time, and difference in modality) and four for quantified (adding difference in quantity) is maintained.

Checkpoint
According to al-Farabi's reduction, what is the single condition necessary for contradiction?
A) Unity of subject
B) Unity of predicate
C) Unity of predicative relation
D) Unity of time

Key Takeaway
All eight conditions for contradiction reduce to one: unity of the predicative relation, by the logical operation of contrapositive.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the pair: 'The Quran is created (makhluq)' and 'The Quran is not created (ghayr makhluq)'. According to the unity of predicative relation, check whether these are genuine contradictions. Assume the subject and predicate are the same in both. What condition must be verified?
?
Take a jadal example: 'Salah is obligatory on every Muslim who is sane and adult' and 'Salah is not obligatory on a Muslim who is insane'. Identify the predicative relation in each and determine if they are the same or different.

Immediate Inference
advanced
8 min
Reducing Conditions for Contradiction: From Eight to One
Critical refinement of conditions for contradiction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct al-Fārābī's reduction of contradiction conditions to three, critique it via al-Abharī's objection, and apply the ultimate reduction to unity of the relational judgment.

Core Idea
All conditions for contradiction reduce to one: unity in the relational judgment.

In classical Islamic logic, eight conditions were traditionally required for two propositions to be genuine contradictions. Al-Fārābī boldly reduced these to just three—subject, predicate, and time—and later even to a single condition: unity of the relational judgment (al-nisba al-ḥukmiyya). In this lesson, we will walk through his reasoning, examine a key objection, and see how this refinement deepens our understanding of logical contradiction. This is not mere abstraction; it directly affects how we test for contradiction in theological and legal arguments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the eight traditional conditions for contradiction
Start by recalling or inferring the eight conditions (e.g., unity of subject, predicate, time, place, relation, etc.). The passage mentions 'these eight' and focuses on subject, predicate, time, and place.
The eight are typically: subject, predicate, time, place, condition, relation, part/whole, potential/actual. Al-Fārābī reduces them.
2
Reconstruct al-Fārābī's reduction to three conditions
Al-Fārābī claims that unity of subject, predicate, and time suffice because the remaining conditions are subsumed. For example, a change in place changes the predicate. Find where he says this in the passage and note the rationale: necessary knowledge that a predicate and its negation cannot both be true at the same time for the same subject.
This reduction is based on the idea that if place differs, the predicate effectively differs.
3
Analyze al-Abharī's objection
Al-Muḥaqqaq al-Abharī objects: if place is subsumed under predicate because a change in place yields a different predicate (e.g., 'eclipse at interposition' vs. 'eclipse at quadrature'), then by the same logic, a change in time yields a different predicate, thus time should also be subsumed under predicate. This would reduce conditions to only two: subject and predicate.
This objection challenges the necessity of a separate time condition.
4
Examine the final reduction to one condition: unity of relational judgment
The author then reports al-Fārābī's further step: all conditions reduce to unity of the relational judgment (al-nisba al-ḥukmiyya). The argument: any difference in subject, predicate, or time changes the relation between them. Therefore, if the relation is the same, all other conditions must be the same. This single condition suffices for contradiction.
This is a powerful unifying principle: the relation itself determines all other aspects.
5
Apply the three-condition framework to quantified propositions
The passage notes that for particular propositions, three conditions (terms, time, modality) suffice, while quantified propositions require an additional condition of difference in quantity to avoid false contradictions. Understand why quantification adds a layer.
For example, 'All A are B' and 'Some A are not B' are not contradictory unless quantity differs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وادعى الفارابي : الاكتفاء بامور ثلاثة من هذه الثمانية وهي وحدة الموضوع و المحمول والزمان، لان العلم الضروري حاصل بان ثبوت المحمول الواحد المعين للموضوع الواحد المعين في زمان معين وانتقائه عنه في عين ذلك الزمان مما لا يصدقان معاً ولا يكذبان والا لما تبعه في ذلك، فادرج باقي الوحدات في وحدة الموضوع والمحمول. قال المحقق الابهرى ما ذكروه لبيان اندراج وحدة المكان في وحدة المحمول فهو بعينه تقتضي اندراج وحدة الزمان في وحدة المحمول لانا اذا قلنا القمر منخسف وقت حيلولة الارض بينه وبين الشمس و القمر ليس بمنخسف وقت التربيع بين النيرين كان المحمولان متغايرين ضرورة تغاير الانحساف وقت الحيلولة للانخساف وقت التربيع فكان يجب ان لا يعتبر اتحاد الموضوع و المحمول. هذا كلامه والامركيا ذكره. والامام ايضاً صرح بذلك في كتاب الآيات والبينات الكبير حيث قال: ان اشتراط وحدة الزمان مندرجة تحت وحدة المحمول الا انهم انها اعتبروا وحدة الزمان بالاستقلال لان كنه الأمر في التناقض وحدة، فالتصريح بهما يوجب زيادة الموضوع والاطلاع على رعايتهما يجب رعايته فيه . وقد ينقل عن الفارابي انه ذكر في بعض تصانيفه انه يمكن رد الشرايط كلها الى شرط واحد وهو الاتحاد في النسبة الحكمية لان اختلاف احدما ذكرنا من الامور موجب لاختلاف النسبة الحكمية اما اذا كان الاختلاف في الموضوع فلان نسبة الشيء الى احد المتغايرين غير نسبته الى المغاير الاخر واما اذا كان فى المحمول فلان نسبة احد المتغايرين الى الشيء غير نسبة الآخر اليه و اما اذا كان فى الزمان فلان نسبته الى غيره في احد الزمانين غير نسبة ذلك الشيء الى ذلك الغير فى الزمان الآخر و هكذا الكلام في البواقي وجميع هذه المقدمات ظاهر واذا ثبت ان اختلاف احد الامور موجب لاختلاف النسبة الحكمية ينعكس بعكس النقيض الى ان اتحاد النسبة الحكمية موجب لاتحاد الامور واذا كان كذلك فنقول : المعتبر في صحة التناقض اتحاد النسبة على معنى ان السلب يجب ان يكون وارداً على عين النسبة التي بها الحكم في الموجبة وبذلك كفاية في المخصوصات والمحصورات. نعم الواردنا ان تعتبر التفصيل المفيد لزيادة الوضوح جعلنا الشرايط فى المخصوصات ثلاثة اتحاد الطرفين واتحاد الزمان والاختلاف بالضرورة واللاضرورة وبالجملة بالجهة و في المحصورات هذه الثلاثة مع الاختلاف بالكمية.
Al-Fārābī claimed: sufficiency of three things from these eight: unity of subject, predicate, and time, because necessary knowledge is obtained that affirmation of one specific predicate for one specific subject in a specific time and its negation about that same time cannot both be true nor both false, otherwise he would not have been followed in that. So he included the remaining unities under the unity of subject and predicate. Al-Muḥaqqiq al-Abharī said: what they mentioned to show the inclusion of unity of place under unity of predicate itself requires the inclusion of unity of time under unity of predicate, because if we say 'the moon is eclipsed at the time of the earth's interposition between it and the sun' and 'the moon is not eclipsed at the time of quadrature of the two luminaries' the two predicates are necessarily different because of the difference of the eclipse at the time of interposition from the eclipse at the time of quadrature, so it would be necessary that unity of subject and predicate not be considered. This is his statement and the matter is as he mentioned. Al-Imām also stated this explicitly in Kitāb al-Āyāt wa al-Bayyināt al-Kabīr when he said: the condition of unity of time is subsumed under unity of predicate, but they considered unity of time independently because the essence of contradiction is unity, so making them explicit increases clarity and attention to their observance must be observed in it. And it is reported from al-Fārābī that he mentioned in some of his works that all conditions can be reduced to one condition: unity in the relational judgment, because difference in any of the mentioned matters necessitates difference in the relational judgment. If the difference is in the subject, then the relation of a thing to one of two different things is not the same as its relation to the other. If it is in the predicate, then the relation of one of the two different things to the thing is not the same as the relation of the other to it. If it is in time, then the relation of something to another in one time is not the same as the relation of that thing to that other in another time. And so on for the rest, and all these premises are evident. If it is established that difference in any of these matters necessitates difference in the relational judgment, then by contrapositive the unity of the relational judgment necessitates unity of the matters. If this is so, we say: the condition for the validity of contradiction is unity of the relation in the sense that the negation must bear upon the very relation by which the judgment is made in the affirmative, and this suffices for particular and quantified propositions. Yes, we intended to consider the detailed division to increase clarity: we made conditions for particular propositions three: unity of the two terms, unity of time, and difference in necessity and non-necessity—in summary, modality—and for quantified propositions these three together with difference in quantity.
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage is a critical examination of al-Fārābī's reduction of the eight conditions for contradiction to three: unity of subject, predicate, and time. The author first presents al-Fārābī's claim that necessary knowledge shows that a predicate's affirmation and negation about the same subject at the same time cannot be both true or both false, so the other five conditions (place, relation, etc.) are subsumed under these three. Al-Muḥaqqaq al-Abharī then objects: if place is subsumed under predicate because a change in place changes the predicate (e.g., 'eclipse at interposition' vs. 'eclipse at quadrature'), the same reasoning should subsume time under predicate, since a change in time also changes the predicate. This would eliminate time as a separate condition. Al-Imām (Fakhr al-Dīn al-Rāzī) confirms this, stating that time is indeed subsumed under predicate, but logicians kept it separate for clarity. Then a report from al-Fārābī goes further: all conditions reduce to one: unity of the relational judgment (al-nisba al-ḥukmiyya). This is proven by showing that any difference in subject, predicate, time, etc., changes the judgment relation, so unity of relation necessitates unity of all conditions. Finally, the author explains the practical application: for particular propositions, three conditions suffice (terms, time, modality), and for quantified propositions, an additional condition of quantity difference is needed to avoid contradiction. The discussion focuses on logical precision, using examples like the moon's eclipse to illustrate how predicates change with time and place.

القضية
المحمول
الموضوع

Key Takeaway
All conditions for logical contradiction ultimately reduce to the single requirement that the negation must bear upon the very same relational judgment as the affirmation.

Predicate Unity Encompasses All Qualifiers in Contradiction
Author refutes objections to the conditions of contradiction by subsuming additional unities under predicate unity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify why additional conditions like cause and instrument are not independent but are subsumed under predicate unity in a contradiction.

Core Idea
Every qualifier of the predicate is part of the predicate itself for contradiction.

In logic, for two propositions to contradict, they must share the same subject, predicate, and time. But what about other unities like cause, instrument, or object? Some object that these must also be unified. The author here refines the condition by showing that these are not separate—they are already part of the predicate. This lesson unpacks that critical refinement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two objections
The passage presents two objections: (1) a contradiction seems to occur without unified time (Zayd is father yesterday vs. not today), and (2) beyond time, unities of cause, instrument, object, and specifying condition are needed. Read the Arabic and translation to spot these.
2
Analyze the first objection (time)
The objector claims that 'Zayd is father of Amr yesterday' and 'He is not his father today' are contradictory even though time differs. The author refutes this: fatherhood is permanent, so if it existed yesterday, it exists today. Thus the second statement is false if the first is true—they are not genuinely contradictory.
This shows that the time condition is not violated because the nature of the predicate matters; the objection is based on a material flaw.
3
Analyze the second objection (additional unities)
The objector lists examples: cause (carpenter works for sultan vs. populace), instrument (writer with Wasiti pen vs. iron pen), object (beater of Amr vs. Bakr), specifying condition (twenty dirhams vs. dinars). The claim is that without unifying these, no contradiction.
These examples seem to challenge the sufficiency of subject, predicate, and time unity.
4
Understand the author's response
The author says these unities are 'included in the unity of the predicate' (داخلة في وحدة المحمول). For each example, the predicate includes its complement: 'worker' implies its beneficiary, 'writer' implies the instrument, etc. So changing the complement changes the predicate entirely.
Thus the condition of predicate unity already ensures these are unified when contradicting.
5
Apply to a new Islamic example
Take a fiqh example: 'Zakat on gold is obligatory at 2.5%' and 'Zakat on gold is not obligatory at 2.5%'. If you add a condition like 'Zakat on gold is obligatory for the wealthy' vs. 'Zakat on gold is not obligatory for the poor', the predicate ('obligatory for...') differs. This shows the principle.
Practice identifying when a qualifier changes the predicate vs. when it is incidental.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان قلت : قد يتحقق التناقض في مثل قولنا زيد اب لعمر وامس وليس باب له اليوم مع عدم اتحاد الزمان. قلت: لانسلم تحقق التناقض فيه لان صدق احديهما وكذب الاخرى ليس لذات الاختلاف بل الخصوص المادة وذلك ، لان الابوة صفة لو تحققت امس تحققت اليوم. فان قلت ايضاً لا يكفى فى تحقق التناقض اتحاد الطرفين و اتحاد الزمان بل يجب ان يتحقق بعض الوحدات ايضاً كوحدة العلة و الألة والمفعول به والمميز والا لم يتحقق التناقض كما اذا قلنا: النجار عامل ای للسلطان وليس بعامل اى للرعية وزيد كاتب اى بالقلم الواسطى وليس بكاتب اي بالحديد و زید ضارب:ای عمراً وليس بضارب اى بكراً وعندى عشرون اى در هماً و ليس عندي عشرون اي ديناراً. قلت هذه الوحدات داخلة في وحدة المحمول لان المحمول فى النجار عامل مع متعلقه و هكذا في البواقي.
If you say: Contradiction may occur in statements like 'Zayd is father of Amr yesterday' and 'He is not his father today' without unity of time. I say: We do not concede that contradiction occurs here, because the truth of one and the falsity of the other is not due to the difference [in time] itself but to the specific material, because fatherhood is a property that if it existed yesterday exists today. If you also say: For contradiction it is not sufficient to have unity of the two terms and unity of time; rather some other unities must also obtain, such as unity of cause, instrument, object, and specifying condition, otherwise contradiction would not occur—as if we say: 'The carpenter is a worker for the sultan' and 'He is not a worker for the populace'; 'Zayd is a writer with the Wasiti pen' and 'He is not a writer with the iron pen'; 'Zayd is a beater of 'Amr' and 'He is not a beater of Bakr'; 'I have twenty dirhams' and 'I do not have twenty dinars'. I say: These unities are included under the unity of the predicate, because the predicate in 'the carpenter is a worker' includes its complement, and so on for the rest.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage presents two objections to the conditions for contradiction and their answers. The first objection: a statement about Zayd being a father yesterday and not being a father today seems to be a contradiction without unified time. The answer: this is not a real contradiction because the truth of one and falsity of the other is not due to time difference but to the nature of fatherhood—if it existed yesterday, it necessarily exists today (since fatherhood is permanent). So the two statements are not genuinely contradictory; rather the second would be false if the first is true. The second objection: beyond unity of subject, predicate, and time, one must also unify cause (e.g., the authority for whom the carpenter works), instrument (the pen), object (the person beaten), and specifying condition (dirhams vs. dinars). The answer: all these are included within the predicate itself. For example, 'the carpenter is a worker for the sultan' has a predicate that includes 'for the sultan'; changing that changes the predicate. Thus they are not separate conditions but part of predicate unity. This shows the thoroughness of the condition of predicate unity.

وحدة العلة

Key Takeaway
The condition of predicate unity in contradiction is comprehensive: any qualifier (cause, instrument, object, etc.) is part of the predicate, so no separate conditions are needed.

The Critique of the Definition of Naqīḍ (Contradictory)
Author critiques the standard definition of naqīḍ and discusses logical implications.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and evaluate the logical objections to the definition of naqīḍ as 'raf' kull shay'' and explain the distinction between simple and modified propositions in determining contradictories.

Core Idea
The definition of contradictory is not simple; it depends on how negation is parsed in the proposition.

In this passage, al-Sharīf al-Jurjānī and subsequent logicians critically examine the standard definition of 'naqīḍ' (contradictory). They reveal hidden complexities: whether the contradictory of a negative is its affirmation or its own negation, and how the parsing of the negative phrase affects the result. Understanding this debate sharpens your ability to handle immediate inferences in Islamic logic.

Guided Path
1
Locate the standard definition under critique
Find the phrase 'نقيض كل شيء رفعه' (the contradictory of everything is its negation). This is the definition that al-Sharīf and others question.
2
Identify al-Sharīf's objection
Al-Sharīf argues that negation (salb) itself is a proposition, and its contradictory is affirmation (ījāb), not the negation of negation. So the definition should be 'رفع كل شيء نقيضه' (the negation of everything is its contradictory).
He suggests redefining to avoid the issue.
3
Understand the objection about double negation
An objector points out that if we adopt 'رفع كل شيء نقيضه', then the contradictory of 'Zayd is not-standing' would be 'Zayd is not not-standing', but these two do not differ in quality (both are negative in a sense). Also, negation would have two contradictories (its own negation and affirmation).
This threatens the standard conditions for contradiction.
4
Analyze the response with the distinction between modified and simple propositions
The response distinguishes two ways to parse 'Zayd is not-standing'. If taken as a simple negative, its contradictory is the simple affirmative 'Zayd is standing'. If the negation particle is part of the predicate (making it an affirmative with a negated predicate), then its contradictory is a simple negative with a negated predicate 'Zayd is not not-standing'. Thus no problem arises.
This shows the importance of parsing in logic.
5
Examine the final argument about the reciprocity of contradiction
A later commentator argues that the relation of contradiction is reciprocal, so if negation is the contradictory of affirmation, then affirmation is the contradictory of negation. Claiming that the negation of negation is identical to affirmation is forced and ignores the difference in conception.
This reinforces that the definition must preserve reciprocity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۳) قوله: «اعلم ان نقيض كل شيء رفعه ... هكذا عرفه غير واحد و قال المحقق الشريف في حواشيه على الشرح المشهور للرسالة الشمسية: «فيه مناقشة لان السلب شيء و نقيضه الايجاب وليس الايجاب رفع السلب و ان كان مستلزماً له بل السلب رفع الايجاب فالاولى ان يقال: رفع كل شيء نقيضه الا ان يراد بالرفع ما هواعم من الرفع حقيقة او ما يساويه .انتهى . واورد عليه بانه لو قيل: رفع كل شيء نقيضه للزم ان يكون قولنا : ما زيد ليس بقائم و نحوه نقيض قولنا زيد ليس بقائم و نحوه ضرورة انه يصدق عليه انه رفعه مع أنهم اشترطوا في التناقض الاختلاف في الكيف كما مر و لا اختلاف وأيضا يلزم ان يكون للسلب نقيضان احدهما رفع السلب والآخر الايجاب. واجيب بانانسلم ذلك ولا يلزم محذور فان السلب ما لم يفرض ثبوته لم يتصور سلبه ضرورة ورود السلب على الايجاب فح يصير قولنا : زيد ليس بقائم و نحوه اذا اريد سلبه موجبة معدولة المحمول لا سالبة محصلة وقولنا ما زيد ليس بقائم فى سلبه سالبة محصلة معدولة المحمول واختلافهما في الكيف بديهي وظاهر أيضاً ان الايجاب انما هو نقيض السالبة المحصلة لا للموجبة المعدولة المحمول. والحاصل ان قولنا زيد ليس بقائم و نحوه اذا لوحظ فيه معنى السلب يكون نقيضه موجبة محصلة فقط و اذالم يلاحظ فيه ذلك بل جعل اداة السلب جزء من المحمول والمجموع ثابتاً للموضوع يكون نقيضه سالبة محصلة معدولة المحمول لاغير فلا يلزم شيء من الأمرين. وقد يجاب عن الاخير باتالانسلم ان الايجاب نقيض حقيقى للسلب بل نقيضه الحقيقى رفعه و انما اطلقوا اسم النقيض عليه تجوزاً ولو سلم فاناندعى الاتحاد والعينية بين رفع السلب و الايجاب. وفيه ان الظاهر ان اطلاق النقيض عليه حقيقة، ضرورة ان رفع الايجاب نقيض له حقيقة وهو يقتضى ان يكون العكس ايضاً كذلك ، بداهة ان كون احد المفهومين نقيضاً للآخر، يستلزم كون الاخرايضاً نقيضاً له وادعاء الاتحاد بينهما لا يخلو عن تعسف وارتكاب خلاف ضرورة تغايرهما فان رفع السلب يتوقف على تصور السلب دون الايجاب فتأمل حق التأمل. (ميرزا محمد علی) (۱۴) قوله: (فنقيض ضرورة الايجاب ... تفريع لما سبق يعنى انه اذاثبت ان نقيض قضية
(13) His statement: 'Know that the contradictory (naqīḍ) of everything is its negation (raf')...'—this is how many defined it. Al-Muḥaqqiq al-Sharīf said in his glosses on the famous commentary of al-Risāla al-Shamsiyya: 'There is a discussion in it, because negation is something and its contradictory is affirmation, and affirmation is not the negation of negation, even if it is entailed by it; rather negation is the negation of affirmation. So it is better to say: The negation of everything is its contradictory, unless by 'negation' is meant what is more general than real negation or what is equivalent to it.' End. It was objected to that if it is said 'The negation of everything is its contradictory,' then it would follow that our statement 'Zayd is not not-standing' and the like would be the contradictory of our statement 'Zayd is not-standing' and the like, necessarily because it is true that it is its negation, even though they have conditioned in contradiction difference in quality as has passed, and there is no difference. Also it would follow that negation has two contradictories: one is the negation of negation, and the other is affirmation. And it was answered: We do not concede that, and no problem follows. For negation, as long as it is not assumed to be established, its negation cannot be conceived, necessarily because negation bears upon affirmation. So our statement 'Zayd is not-standing' and the like, when its negation is intended, becomes an affirmative with a negated predicate (mawjūba maʿdūlat al-maḥmūl), not a simple negative. And our statement 'Zayd is not not-standing' in its negation is a simple negative with a negated predicate (sāliba muḥaṣṣala maʿdūlat al-maḥmūl). Their difference in quality is obvious. It is also apparent that affirmation is only the contradictory of the simple negative, not of the affirmative with a negated predicate. In summary, our statement 'Zayd is not-standing' and the like: if the meaning of negation is considered in it, its contradictory is only a simple affirmative; if that is not considered but the negation tool is made part of the predicate and the whole is affirmed of the subject, then its contradictory is a simple negative with a negated predicate only, so neither of the two [problems] follows. And it may be answered about the latter by: We do not concede that affirmation is the real contradictory of negation; rather its real contradictory is its negation. They only used the term 'contradictory' for it metaphorically. Even if granted, we do not claim identity and sameness between the negation of negation and affirmation. But in it [there is the consideration] that apparently the application of 'contradictory' to it is real, necessarily because the negation of affirmation is its contradictory in reality, and that requires that the converse also be so, by the evident fact that one concept being the contradictory of another necessitates that the other is also its contradictory. Claiming identity between them is not free from arbitrariness and going against the evident fact of their difference, for the negation of negation depends on conceiving negation without affirmation. So reflect carefully. (Mīrzā Muḥammad ʿAlī) (14) His statement: 'So the contradictory of the necessary affirmation...' is a corollary of what preceded, meaning that when it is established that the contradictory of a proposition...
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage critically examines the definition of 'naqīḍ' (contradictory) as 'raf' kull shay'' (the negation of everything). The standard definition is that the contradictory of a proposition is its negation. Al-Sharīf al-Jurjānī objects: negation itself is a proposition, and its contradictory is affirmation, not the negation of negation. He suggests redefining 'naqīḍ' as the negation of something, but warns about ambiguity. An objection is raised: if we say 'the negation of everything is its contradictory', then 'Zayd is not not-standing' would be the contradictory of 'Zayd is not-standing', but they are not opposite in quality (both are negative in a sense). Also, negation would have two contradictories. The response distinguishes between two interpretations: if 'Zayd is not-standing' is taken as a simple negative, its contradictory is the simple affirmative 'Zayd is standing'. If the negative particle is part of the predicate (making it an affirmative with a negated predicate), then its contradictory is a simple negative with a negated predicate ('Zayd is not not-standing'). Thus no problem arises. Another response denies that affirmation is the real contradictory of negation; rather the real contradictory of negation is the removal of that negation (which is an affirmative). The passage ends with a note that the contradictory relation is reciprocal; claiming identity between 'removal of negation' and 'affirmation' is forced. The commentary includes a citation from Mīrzā Muḥammad ʿAlī. This is a sophisticated logical discussion about the nature of contradiction and the definition of a fundamental term.

Conditions for Contradiction: Unity of Predicate Includes All Relational Complements
Author refutes objections about additional conditions for contradiction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the full conditions for logical contradiction (tanāquḍ) and explain why unity of predicate subsumes unity of cause, instrument, object, and specification.

Core Idea
True contradiction requires unity of subject, predicate, and time — but the predicate's unity includes all its relational complements.

In this passage, the author refutes two objections to the standard conditions for contradiction. The objector first argues that contradiction can occur without unity of time, then claims that additional unities (cause, instrument, etc.) are needed. The author shows that both objections fail because the predicate, when properly understood, includes its relevant complements. This lesson will guide you through parsing this dialectical exchange and understanding the precise conditions for tanāquḍ.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objector's first claim
The objector says contradiction can occur even when time differs, using 'Zayd was a father yesterday and is not a father today'. Note that the two statements differ in time but have same subject and predicate.
The objector is challenging the condition of unity of time.
2
Analyze the author's first reply
The author denies contradiction because the truth of one and falsehood of the other is not due to a logical difference but to a material one: fatherhood, once established, persists. So the statements are not genuinely contradictory — they merely reflect a change in the subject's state.
The author distinguishes formal vs. material difference.
3
Identify the objector's second claim
The objector introduces additional unities needed: cause, instrument, object, specification. Examples: 'carpenter is a worker for the sultan' vs. 'not a worker for the subjects'; 'Zayd is a writer with the Wasiti pen' vs. 'not with the iron pen'; etc.
The objector thinks these show that time and subject-predicate unity are insufficient.
4
Understand the author's second reply
The author says these unities are already included in unity of the predicate, because the predicate in such propositions includes its complement (muta‘alliq). So the standard conditions (subject, predicate, time) are sufficient.
The predicate 'worker' is ambiguous without specifying for whom; once the complement is specified, the predicate is unified.
5
Apply the rule: test a new example
Given a proposition pair like 'The qadi judged according to Hanafi law' and 'The qadi did not judge according to Shafi'i law', determine if it is a contradiction. Answer: No, because the predicate 'judged' differs in its complement (Hanafi vs. Shafi'i), so the predicate is not unified.
Unity of predicate requires unity of all qualifiers implicitly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان قلت: قد يتحقق التناقض في مثل قولنا زيد أب لعمر أمس وليس بأب له اليوم مع عدم اتحاد الزمان. قلت: لا نسلم تحقق التناقض فيه لأن صدق إحديهما وكذب الأخرى ليس لذات الاختلاف بل لخصوص المادة وذلك لأن الأبوة صفة لو تحققت أمس تحققت اليوم. فان قلت أيضاً لا يكفي في تحقق التناقض اتحاد الطرفين واتحاد الزمان بل يجب أن يتحقق بعض الوحدات أيضاً كوحدة العلة والآلة والمفعول به والمميز وإلا لم يتحقق التناقض كما إذا قلنا: النجار عامل أي للسلطان وليس بعامل أي للرعية، وزيد كاتب أي بالقلم الواسطي وليس بكاتب أي بالحديد، وزيد ضارب أي عمراً وليس بضارب أي بكراً، وعندي عشرون أي درهماً وليس عندي عشرون أي ديناراً. قلت: هذه الوحدات داخلة في وحدة المحمول لأن المحمول في النجار عامل مع متعلقه وهكذا في البواقي.
If you say: Contradiction may occur in our statement 'Zayd was a father to Amr yesterday and is not a father to him today' without unity of time. I say: We do not accept that contradiction occurs therein because the truth of one and falsehood of the other is not due to the essence of the difference but to the particularity of the material, and that is because fatherhood is an attribute which, if it existed yesterday, exists today. If you also say: The unity of the two extremes and unity of time are not sufficient for the occurrence of contradiction; rather some other unities must also occur, such as unity of cause, instrument, object, and specification; otherwise contradiction would not occur, as when we say: The carpenter is a worker (i.e., for the sultan) and is not a worker (i.e., for the subjects), and Zayd is a writer (i.e., with the Wasiti pen) and is not a writer (i.e., with the iron pen), and Zayd is a beater (i.e., of Amr) and is not a beater (i.e., of Bakr), and I have twenty (i.e., dirhams) and I do not have twenty (i.e., dinars). I say: These unities are included in the unity of the predicate, because the predicate in 'the carpenter is a worker' includes its complement, and similarly for the rest.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical exchange (Q&A) regarding the conditions for logical contradiction (tanāquḍ). The objector first suggests that contradiction can occur even when time is not unified, citing the example 'Zayd was a father yesterday and is not a father today.' The author refutes this by explaining that fatherhood, once established, persists; thus the apparent difference is not a true logical contradiction but a material one — the judgments differ because the subject's state has changed materially, not formally. The objector then raises a second objection: contradiction requires more than unity of subject, predicate, and time; it also requires unity of cause, instrument, object, and specification. Examples are given: 'the carpenter is a worker for the sultan' vs. 'not a worker for the subjects', where the predicate 'worker' is ambiguous without its complement. The author responds that these additional unities are actually subsumed under unity of the predicate, because the predicate in such propositions includes its relevant complement (muta‘alliq). Thus the condition for contradiction remains the standard one: unity of subject, predicate, time, and (implicitly) all relational qualifiers. The passage illustrates how technical discussions in Islamic logic refine the classical conditions for tanāquḍ by considering qarā’in (contextual qualifications).

Key Terms
التناقض
الوحدة
المحمول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
True logical contradiction requires more than just opposite truth values; the subject, predicate, time, and all predicate complements must be unified, with the latter being encompassed by unity of the predicate.

Refining the Definition of Contradictory (Naqīḍ)
Author presents and critiques the definition of naqīḍ as 'raising something', then defends it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to critically evaluate the definition of naqīḍ as 'negation of something' by identifying the objections raised and the refined understanding involving the distinction between a simple negative and an affirmative with negated predicate.

Core Idea
The definition of contradictory must account for mutual relation; otherwise, negation itself would have two contradictories.

The standard definition of naqīḍ as 'the negation of everything' seems straightforward, but al-Sharīf and others show it leads to paradoxes. In this lesson, we dissect these objections and the ingenious resolution involving the distinction between a simple negative (sālaba muḥaṣṣala) and an affirmative with negated predicate (mūjaba ma‘dūlat al-maḥmūl).

Guided Path
1
State the initial definition
Read the opening line: 'اعلم أن نقيض كل شيء رفعه' (Know that the naqīḍ of everything is its negation). This is the definition under critique.
2
Identify al-Sharīf's objection
Al-Sharīf points out that negation (salb) itself is a thing, and its contradictory is affirmation (ījāb), not the negation of negation. He suggests rephrasing to avoid circularity.
Notice the shift in perspective: the definiendum 'negation of a thing' treats negation as an operator, but when the thing is itself a negation, problems arise.
3
Analyze the two objections against the original definition
Objection 1: If naqīḍ is negation, then 'What is Zayd not standing?' would be the naqīḍ of 'Zayd is not standing', but they have the same quality (negative), violating the condition of difference in quality. Objection 2: A single proposition would have two naqīḍs: its negation and its affirmation.
These objections highlight the need for precision about what 'negation' means in context.
4
Understand the resolution via two readings
The response distinguishes two ways to read a negative proposition like 'Zayd is not standing': (a) as a simple negative (sālaba muḥaṣṣala) where negation attaches to the copula – its contradictory is a simple affirmative; (b) as an affirmative with negated predicate (mūjaba ma‘dūlat al-maḥmūl) where the negation is part of the predicate – its contradictory is a simple negative with a negated predicate. This resolves the twin problems.
This distinction preserves the rule that contradictories differ in quality: in (a) quality flips, in (b) quality remains but the predicate changes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعلم أن نقيض كل شيء رفعه... هكذا عرفه غير واحد. وقال المحقق الشريف في حواشيه على الشرح المشهور للرسالة الشمسية: «فيه مناقشة لأن السلب شيء ونقيضه الإيجاب وليس الإيجاب رفع السلب وإن كان مستلزماً له بل السلب رفع الإيجاب فالأولى أن يقال: رفع كل شيء نقيضه إلا أن يراد بالرفع ما هو أعم من الرفع حقيقة أو ما يساويه». انتهى. وأورد عليه بأنه لو قيل: رفع كل شيء نقيضه للزم أن يكون قولنا: ما زيد ليس بقائم ونحوه نقيض قولنا زيد ليس بقائم ونحوه ضرورة أنه يصدق عليه أنه رفعه مع أنهم اشترطوا في التناقض الاختلاف في الكيف كما مر ولا اختلاف. وأيضاً يلزم أن يكون للسلب نقيضان أحدهما رفع السلب والآخر الإيجاب. وأجيب بأنه لا نسلم ذلك ولا يلزم محذور، فإن السلب ما لم يفرض ثبوته لم يتصور سلبه ضرورة ورود السلب على الإيجاب فح يصير قولنا: زيد ليس بقائم ونحوه إذا أريد سلبه موجبة معدولة المحمول لا سالبة محصلة، وقولنا ما زيد ليس بقائم في سلبه سالبة محصلة معدولة المحمول واختلافهما في الكيف بديهي. وظاهر أيضاً أن الإيجاب إنما هو نقيض السالبة المحصلة لا للموجبة المعدولة المحمول. والحاصل أن قولنا زيد ليس بقائم ونحوه إذا لوحظ فيه معنى السلب يكون نقيضه موجبة محصلة فقط، وإذا لم يلاحظ فيه ذلك بل جعل أداة السلب جزءاً من المحمول والمجموع ثابتاً للموضوع يكون نقيضه سالبة محصلة معدولة المحمول لا غير فلا يلزم شيء من الأمرين. وقد يجاب عن الأخير بأنه لا نسلم أن الإيجاب نقيض حقيقي للسلب بل نقيضه الحقيقي رفعه وإنما أطلقوا اسم النقيض عليه تجوزاً. ولو سلم فإنا ندعي الاتحاد والعينية بين رفع السلب والإيجاب. وفيه أن الظاهر أن إطلاق النقيض عليه حقيقة، ضرورة أن رفع الإيجاب نقيض له حقيقة وهو يقتضي أن يكون العكس أيضاً كذلك، بداهة أن كون أحد المفهومين نقيضاً للآخر يستلزم كون الآخر أيضاً نقيضاً له، وادعاء الاتحاد بينهما لا يخلو عن تعسف وارتكاب خلاف ضرورة تغايرهما، فإن رفع السلب يتوقف على تصور السلب دون الإيجاب. فتأمل حق التأمل. (ميرزا محمد علي)
Know that the naqīḍ (contradictory) of everything is its negation (raf‘)... This is how more than one defined it. Al-Muḥaqqiq al-Sharīf said in his glosses on the famous commentary of al-Risāla al-Shamsiyya: 'There is a discussion (in it) because negation (salb) is a thing and its naqīḍ is affirmation (ījāb), and affirmation is not the negation of negation, although it entails it. Rather negation is the negation of affirmation. So it is better to say: The negation of everything is its naqīḍ, unless by negation is meant what is more general than negation in reality or what is equal to it.' End. And it was objected to it that if it were said: The negation of everything is its naqīḍ, then our statement 'What is Zayd not standing?' and the like would be the naqīḍ of our statement 'Zayd is not standing' and the like, necessarily because it would be true that it is its negation, even though they required in contradiction difference in quality as mentioned, and there is no difference. Also, it would entail that negation has two naqīḍs: one is the negation of negation and the other is affirmation. And it was answered that we do not accept that, and no absurdity follows, because negation is not conceptualized as negated unless its existence is supposed, necessarily because negation occurs to affirmation. Thus our statement 'Zayd is not standing' and the like, when its negation is intended, becomes an affirmative with a negated predicate (mawjūba ma‘dūlat al-maḥmūl), not a simple negative (sālaba muḥaṣṣala). And our statement 'What is Zayd not standing?' in its negation is a simple negative with a negated predicate, and their difference in quality is obvious. It is also apparent that affirmation is only the naqīḍ of the simple negative, not of the affirmative with negated predicate. In sum, our statement 'Zayd is not standing' and the like, if the meaning of negation is observed in it, its naqīḍ is only a simple affirmative; if that is not observed but the negation particle is made part of the predicate and the whole is affirmed of the subject, then its naqīḍ is a simple negative with negated predicate only, so neither of the two problems follows. And it is answered concerning the latter by saying: We do not accept that affirmation is a true naqīḍ of negation; rather its true naqīḍ is its negation, and they only called it naqīḍ figuratively. And if it is accepted, then we claim identity and union between the negation of negation and affirmation. But in it (this answer) is that it is apparent that calling it naqīḍ is real, necessarily because the negation of affirmation is its naqīḍ in reality, and that requires that the reverse also be so, since the fact that one concept is a naqīḍ of another necessitates that the other is also its naqīḍ. And claiming union between them is not free from distortion and contrary to the necessity of their difference, for the negation of negation depends on conceiving negation without affirmation. So ponder carefully. (Mīrzā Muḥammad ‘Alī)
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage is a critical analysis of the standard definition of naqīḍ (contradictory) as 'the negation of a thing' (raf‘ kull shay’). The commentator begins by stating the definition given by many: 'The naqīḍ of everything is its negation.' Al-Muḥaqqiq al-Sharīf objects: negation (salb) is itself a thing; its naqīḍ is affirmation, but affirmation is not the negation of negation (though it entails it). Actually, negation is the negation of affirmation. So a better definition is 'the negation of everything is its naqīḍ', unless 'negation' means something broader. Two serious objections are raised against the original definition. First, if 'negation of X' means 'naqīḍ of X', then 'What is Zayd not standing?' would be the naqīḍ of 'Zayd is not standing' — but these have the same quality (both negative), contradicting the condition that naqīḍ must differ in quality. Second, a single proposition would have two naqīḍs: its negation and its affirmation. The response distinguishes two readings of a negative proposition like 'Zayd is not standing'. If the negation is taken as part of the judgment, its contradictory is 'Zayd is standing' (affirmative). If the negation is made part of the predicate (e.g. 'Zayd is non-standing'), then its contradictory is a negative with a negated predicate (e.g. 'Zayd is not non-standing'). This resolves the double-naqīḍ problem. A further answer claims that affirmation is only figuratively called naqīḍ of negation; the true naqīḍ is the negation of that negation. But the commentator argues that this is artificial — if negation of a negative is the naqīḍ, then by symmetry affirmation must also be a true naqīḍ, since the relation is mutual. The passage exemplifies the meticulous analysis typical of the ḥāshiya tradition, where definitions are tested against concrete counterexamples and alternative interpretations.

Key Terms
النقيض (al-naqīḍ): The contradictory of a proposition, defined initially as 'raf‘ (negation) of the proposition'; debated whether this includes only the simple opposite or also the negation of negation [Note: In earlier logic (e.g., Isāghūjī), naqīḍ is simply the opposite in quality; later ḥāshiyas like this one refine the definition to handle modal and quantified cases.]
الرفع (al-raf‘): Negation or removal; in this context, the act of negating a proposition to form its contradictory [Note: This term is used specifically for the operation of forming a contradictory; in some texts it is equivalent to salb (negation), but here al-Sharīf suggests it might be broader.]
السالبة المحصلة (al-sālaba al-muḥaṣṣala): A simple negative proposition where the negation applies to the copula (e.g., 'Zayd is not standing'), as opposed to a negative where the predicate itself is negated
الموجبة المعدولة المحمول (al-mūjaba al-ma‘dūlat al-maḥmūl): An affirmative proposition with a negated predicate (e.g., 'Zayd is non-standing'), which has a different contradictory from the simple negative

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Zayd is standing.
D) Zayd is non-standing.

Key Takeaway
The definition of naqīḍ requires careful distinction between a simple negative and an affirmative with negated predicate to avoid logical paradoxes.
